201407	36	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	Let me turn over the floor now to Simon for the Desk report.	61	6
201407	37	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	61	6
201407	38	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Over the intermeeting period, domestic financial conditions eased as longer-term interest rates declined and equity prices increased.	61	6
201407	39	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the top-left panel of your first exhibit, markets responded to some better-than-expected labor market data and Federal Reserve communications that focused less on the recent uptick in inflation than some had anticipated.	61	6
201407	40	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Market participants paid particular attention to the discussion of policy normalization in the June FOMC meeting minutes, which reportedly put downward pressure on short-term interest rates.	61	6
201407	41	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Broad US financial markets were little affected, on net, by unfavorable geopolitical developments, though they led to declines in Treasury yields at times.	61	6
201407	42	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	In terms of broader themes, market participants continued to focus on the substantial decline in longer-dated forward rates across advanced economies and the low levels of volatility in financial markets since the beginning of the year.	61	6
201407	43	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	There is also growing attention on the relative stability of the expected federal funds path.	61	6
201407	44	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	The top-right panel shows this path is little changed since December, despite better- than-expected labor market data and shifts higher in the SEP rate projections.	61	6
201407	45	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	At present, the market-implied path lies notably below the median of the June SEP paths.	61	6
201407	46	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	The Desk’s surveys can be used to examine more directly whether aspects of market beliefs on the path of policy have changed more materially despite the relative stability of the market-implied path.	61	6
201407	47	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Since dealers’ and buy-side participants’ responses were not notably different from each other in the most recent surveys, I will focus on the dealer results, for which we have a longer history.	61	6
201407	48	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the middle-left panel, since December the average probability dealers assign to liftoff occurring in 2015 has increased about 25 percentage points.	61	6
201407	49	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Further, the dealers are placing increasingly more weight on liftoff in the first half of 2015.	61	6
201407	50	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	However, views of the pace of tightening thereafter do not seem to have changed much.	61	6
201407	51	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	The middle- right panel shows dealer average responses for the modal pace of tightening after liftoff since the start of 2013.	61	6
201407	52	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	On average, dealers expect the FOMC to tighten about 125 basis points per year for the first two years after liftoff, and there has been little change in this view.	61	6
201407	53	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	The modal pace in the third year is lower, and has declined recently, consistent with the lower expectations for the longer-run neutral rate.	61	6
201407	54	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	One explanation for the recent stability in the modal pace of tightening in the first two years of rate normalization is that market participants’ broad economic outlook is not markedly changed.	61	6
201407	55	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Indeed, while unemployment rate forecasts from the Desk’s and other surveys have markedly declined since December, GDP growth and inflation forecasts for 2015 and 2016 are little changed.	61	6
201407	56	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	With regard to the growing difference between the market-implied path and the SEP  path, contacts have suggested this partly reflects the interpretation of the so-called dots.	61	6
201407	57	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Market participants generally believe that the futures market is priced near the perceived level of the Chair’s projections, which most believe is the 4th to 7th lowest dot.	61	6
201407	58	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	However, there are many market participants who suggest the market as a whole might be overly complacent in forming their expectations for monetary policy amid continued accommodation supported by forward guidance and low market volatility.	61	6
201407	59	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Direct evidence on this issue from market reaction to economic data releases is mixed:  The Tealbook, examining a sample going back to 1990, finds little convincing evidence of excessively low sensitivity to economic news.	61	6
201407	60	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	However, Desk analysis using a smaller sample finds, as does the Tealbook, that the responsiveness of longer-term interest rates to economic data surprises has been lower this year than it was in the prior three years.	61	6
201407	61	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Market prices that could register possible unease about the policy rate path show almost the opposite of concern.	61	6
201407	62	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Measures of fixed-income skew, while still positive, have declined since the start of the year, as shown in the bottom-left panel, suggesting investors in these markets now see less risk of a shift up in rates.	61	6
201407	63	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Additionally, as shown in the bottom-right panel, longer-term measures of inflation compensation are very stable, although shorter-dated measures have increased in recent months along with realized inflation.	61	6
201407	64	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	However, if there was excess complacency in financial markets about the level of longer-term interest rates promoted by the accommodative stance of advanced economy central banks, this complacency might also cause measures of interest rate skew and inflation compensation not to reflect the underlying risks.	61	6
201407	65	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	An alternative explanation for some of the patterns observed in financial markets given by some market participants—not related to complacency but perhaps even more concerning—is that the decline in long-forward rates is partly driven by the risk of a policy error, whereby the Committee will tighten policy before the economy can sustain higher rates, necessitating a subsequent easing of policy back toward the zero bound.	61	6
201407	66	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Your next exhibit reviews international developments over the period.	61	6
201407	67	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	In the UK, market attention focused on recent communications from the Bank of England.	61	6
201407	68	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	These included Governor Carney’s Mansion House speech, in which he stated that a rate hike could happen “sooner than markets currently expect.”	61	6
201407	69	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	This comment prompted an increase in front-end UK interest rates and a modest rise in shorter- dated interest rate implied volatility, as shown in your top-left panel.	61	6
201407	70	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	While these moves partially retraced, following evolving Bank of England commentary, both interest rates and implied volatility remain higher.	61	6
201407	71	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Longer-dated interest rates and equity prices in the UK declined following the speech and remained lower.	61	6
201407	72	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Global risk asset performance was mixed, with US equities outperforming those in Europe over the period, as shown in the top-right panel.	61	6
201407	73	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	European financial markets responded to concerns about the possible imposition of further criminal penalties on European banks, which increased in April following media reports on this topic.	61	6
201407	74	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Since then, the share prices of many of the largest euro-area and UK banks have declined due to increasing uncertainty regarding future litigation and associated penalties.	61	6
201407	75	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	US banks have been less affected by these concerns as market participants view them as more advanced in resolving outstanding litigation.	61	6
201407	76	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Separately, European banking sector concerns escalated further after corporate governance issues and liquidity stresses intensified at Banco Espírito Santo.	61	6
201407	77	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Its shares have fallen more than 50 percent over the intermeeting period, and have damped investor sentiment toward other peripheral banks.	61	6
201407	78	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	These banking concerns and, to a lesser extent, rising geopolitical tensions also contributed to a small widening in euro-area peripheral government bond spreads, as shown in your middle-left panel.	61	6
201407	79	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Similarly, US high-yield corporate spreads widened slightly over the period, in part because of a paring back of investor positions as spreads reached average levels from 2005 to 2007.	61	6
201407	80	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Emerging market asset prices continued to increase despite a marked decline in Russian financial markets, shown in your middle-right panel.	61	6
201407	81	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Prices of Russian assets fell because of a worsened growth outlook, partially as an effect of sanctions related to the Ukraine situation and to fears of further sanctions following the downing of a commercial airplane in Ukraine.	61	6
201407	82	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Spillover of these concerns to other emerging markets was limited as asset price increases likely reflected the ongoing reach for higher-yielding investments amidst low volatility, better-than-expected economic data in China, and continued highly accommodative monetary policy in advanced economies.	61	6
201407	83	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	With regard to the ECB, euro-area money market rates continued to trade at very low or negative levels in the wake of the rate cuts and liquidity measures announced at the June ECB meeting, including the new targeted LTROs, which will begin in September.	61	6
201407	84	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	These so-called TLTROs are intended to incentivize lending to euro-area nonfinancial corporates and households, with contacts estimating up to €850 billion in participation across all eight operations.	61	6
201407	85	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Such usage could result in further modest downward pressure on euro-area money market rates, including the already negative overnight repo rates for French and German collateral shown in the bottom-left panel.	61	6
201407	86	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	The Desk’s management of the SOMA and ESF euro foreign currency reserve portfolio has been affected by these negative money market rates.	61	6
201407	87	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	To minimize the effect of negative rates, the Desk extended the term of some investments.	61	6
201407	88	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	This has caused the portfolio duration to rise very close to the Desk’s 12-month internal limit, as shown in the bottom-right panel.	61	6
201407	89	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	In the current environment, we will continue to face tradeoffs between accepting negative rates and extending duration by investing in longer-dated positive-yielding instruments.	61	6
201407	90	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Depending on the evolution of market rates, the Desk may seek the Committee’s approval to extend the public 18-month duration limit.	61	6
201407	91	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	In domestic operations, usage of the overnight RRP, shown in the top-left panel of your final exhibit, averaged about $130 billion per day over the intermeeting period, about $30 billion lower than in the previous period.	61	6
201407	92	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	The decline was primarily due to decreased demand from money market funds, which had higher-yielding alternatives than last period, when decreases in the supply of Treasury bills put downward pressure on money market rates.	61	6
201407	93	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	However, over quarter-end, overnight RRP take-up reached $339 billion, with nearly $200 billion flowing into the operation on June 30 and exiting on July 1.	61	6
201407	94	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	This large one-day increase reflects the contraction in borrowing activity associated with banks’ and dealers’ behavior around financial reporting dates.	61	6
201407	95	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	As a result, short-term investors, including money funds, have fewer investment opportunities.	61	6
201407	96	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	In the absence of the overnight RRP exercise, these funds would increase their unremunerated balances at custodial banks or invest in other assets at lower and perhaps negative rates.	61	6
201407	97	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	The top-right panel shows some of these dynamics: Reserve balances of foreign banking organizations decrease sharply at quarter-ends as they pare back the size of their balance sheets, while reserve balances at custodial banks rise.	61	6
201407	98	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	The contraction in FBO borrowing activity at quarter-ends has increased as firms prepare to comply with Basel III leverage ratio requirements and excess reserves continue to grow.	61	6
201407	99	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	In addition, this was the first quarter in which balance sheet size will be used to assess whether an FBO will need to form an intermediate holding company and thus become subject to US regulatory requirements.	61	6
201407	100	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	This consideration may have further encouraged dealers owned by foreign financial institutions to shrink their balance sheets.	61	6
201407	101	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Participation in TDF test operations was also influenced by quarter-end dynamics.	61	6
201407	102	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	As you are aware, the staff completed its most recent series of tests, which involved increasing the offered rate over the past four operations.	61	6
201407	103	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the middle-left panel, take-up rose as we offered higher rates, and reached $153 billion in the final operation.	61	6
201407	104	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	The operation that covered quarter-end was an exception to this trend, as some large domestic and foreign participants appeared reluctant to hold term deposits over their regulatory reporting date.	61	6
201407	105	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	As discussed in a memo you received before the meeting, a wide range of banks continue to note that demand for TDF deposits is constrained because of how these deposits effect the LCR.	61	6
201407	106	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	If banks had the option to withdraw funds on a same-day basis prior to maturity, TDF deposits would become LCR-compliant.	61	6
201407	107	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	The staff has developed plans for preliminary testing in late summer or early fall of a variation of the TDF that includes an early withdrawal feature.	61	6
201407	108	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Under such testing, a penalty rate would be charged to firms for breaking a TDF deposit, and it would be set at a level that would make opportunistic withdrawal of funds very unlikely.	61	6
201407	109	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Turning to Treasury markets, as shown in the middle-right panel, fails increased sharply in June, although they were quickly resolved and did not affect broader Treasury market functioning.	61	6
201407	110	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	The increase largely reflected a temporary bout of fails in three of the most recently issued, or “benchmark,” securities.	61	6
201407	111	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Non-public data suggest that large holdings by certain foreign official accounts, which tend not to lend securities, help explain some of the spike in benchmark fails in June.	61	6
201407	112	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Importantly, it does not appear that the fails are related to large SOMA holdings of individual securities.	61	6
201407	113	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	In fact, our holdings often help prevent fails because we make them available to the market through Desk securities lending operations.	61	6
201407	114	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	There has been little change in our securities lending activity despite the rise in fails, largely because recent fails have been concentrated in benchmark securities of which we have few, if any, holdings.	61	6
201407	115	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Some market participants have speculated that changes in the regulatory environment may have made fails more likely, perhaps due to reluctance on the part of dealers to devote their balance sheet to low-margin businesses like repo or securities lending.	61	6
201407	116	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	In the MBS market, lower mortgage rates and increased summer purchase activity led to faster prepayment speeds on the SOMA portfolio, with paydowns increasing from $17 billion in June to $19 billion in July.	61	6
201407	117	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	As a result, reinvestment purchases will exceed the size of outright purchases.	61	6
201407	118	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Following the discussion of reinvestments in the June FOMC minutes, nearly all Desk survey respondents expect the Committee to continue reinvestments until after liftoff.	61	6
201407	119	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	If the Committee reduces the pace of Treasury or MBS purchases at this meeting, as expected by nearly all market participants, we would release a Desk statement at the same time as the Committee statement.	61	6
201407	120	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Lorie and I will have copies of the statement available for review tomorrow.	61	6
201407	121	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Next, I will review the market reaction to the discussion of policy normalization in the June FOMC minutes.	61	6
201407	122	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Prior to the minutes, many market participants anticipated that the overnight RRP and IOER would be the primary tools used to control rates, particularly while the balance sheet is large.	61	6
201407	123	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Market participants now expect overnight RRP to play a more supplementary role.	61	6
201407	124	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Some market participants were surprised that the Committee anticipates a spread between the IOER and ON RRP rates that is near or above its current level.	61	6
201407	125	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Following the minutes, the median expectation for the spread at liftoff seen in the Desk’s surveys shifted from 10 basis points to 20 basis points, as shown in the bottom-left panel.	61	6
201407	126	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Market participants still have dispersed expectations for usage of the ON RRP.	61	6
201407	127	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Among survey respondents who expect the spread between the IOER and ON RRP rates to be 20 basis points, the median expected level of overnight RRP usage at liftoff is $350 billion, down a bit from expectations ahead of the June FOMC.	61	6
201407	128	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Some market participants have argued that ongoing regulatory developments, including recently announced money market fund reforms, could lead to higher average usage in the future.	61	6
201407	129	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Dealers’ expectations for the levels of short-term rates at liftoff appear to have coalesced following the minutes, as shown in the bottom-right panel.	61	6
201407	130	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	The average respondent now expects the effective federal funds rate to trade in the middle of the range created by the IOER and ON RRP rates, rather than near the top of the range.	61	6
201407	131	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Following the discussion in the minutes, most respondents now appear to interpret liftoff as entailing the first increase in IOER rather than just a tightening of the spread between the IOER and ON RRP rates.	61	6
201407	132	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	When we condition on the views of respondents who had a consistent definition of liftoff across the June and July surveys—specifically, the 20 respondents who expected IOER to be 50 basis points, represented by the red dot—we find that expectations for the effective federal funds rate at liftoff declined, on average, 13 basis points between the surveys.	61	6
201407	133	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	This decline is consistent with the market reaction following the release of the minutes.	61	6
201407	134	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Money market rates broadly declined, with rates on Eurodollar futures maturing in late 2015 and early 2016 falling as much as 9 basis points.	61	6
201407	135	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Market participants suggested that both secured and unsecured money market rates may trade lower than previously expected as a result of the wider anticipated spread between the IOER and ON RRP rates.	61	6
201407	136	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Finally, I would like to highlight briefly two distinct counterparty proposals from the Desk.	61	6
201407	137	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	In early August, the Desk is planning to announce a pilot program to extend our MBS trading relationship to a few firms that are too small to qualify as primary dealers, similar to the nearly complete Treasury Operations Counterparty Pilot Program.	61	6
201407	138	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Both pilot programs will provide useful insights into our counterparty framework.	61	6
201407	139	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Second, in a memo you received before the meeting, we discussed that in light of the understanding under which the current extended counterparties in the ON RRP operations were enrolled, the interests of reasonable governance argue for revisiting the counterparty list.	61	6
201407	140	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Specifically, we requested authorization to open an enrollment wave to firms that meet the current eligibility criteria.	61	6
201407	141	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	However, if preferred, we can postpone reopening until the Committee has finalized the normalization principles.	61	6
201407	142	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	61	6
201407	143	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	That concludes my prepared remarks.	61	6

201407	146	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	President Rosengren.	62	6
201407	147	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you.	62	6
201407	148	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Looking at your charts 13 and 14—when I do econometric work I spend a lot of time looking at outliers, and it looks like the end of the quarter has outliers that are relevant for understanding short-term credit behavior.	62	6
201407	149	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	When I think of federal funds, I think it’s a GSE-dominated market.	62	6
201407	150	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	When I think of excess reserves, I think of it as basically a foreign branch–dominated market.	62	6
201407	151	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	I wonder if you could expand a little bit more on the behavior—we have been calling it “window-dressing” in some of the memos, but it might be worth just elaborating a little bit more on what is encouraging the branches to dramatically change toward the end of the quarter, and what would be the implication—are there other ways that we could affect behavior?	62	6
201407	152	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	If we had significant limitations on some of our facilities, are there other alternatives that could make us think about foreign branch behavior at the end of the quarter?	62	6
201407	153	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	My view of what’s going on is that a large amount of the reserves in the system are held at these foreign banks.	62	6
201407	154	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	About 52 to 54 percent is the average.	62	6
201407	155	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Most of the trading in the federal funds market, and also the Eurodollar market, is an arbitrage trade.	62	6
201407	156	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	It is an overnight trade, in which someone who doesn’t have access to interest on excess reserves gives money to a foreign banking organization who can then earn interest on excess reserves.	62	6
201407	157	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	At quarter-end, the easiest way for the foreign banks to reduce their balance sheet is to reduce those excess reserves, because they are not really serving any purpose other than the arbitrage trade.	62	6
201407	158	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	It’s a rather neutral event within financial markets for the foreign banking organizations.	62	6
201407	159	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	It does cause challenges for the investors that they deal with.	62	6
201407	160	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	As you can see, last year what would happen is the custodial balances in big custodian banks would go up at that point, because there wouldn’t be balance sheet available elsewhere.	62	6
201407	161	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	In terms of how we could change this, I’m not completely sure what the economics are behind the window-dressing that happens.	62	6
201407	162	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	It seems that there could be accounting incentives to do it.	62	6
201407	163	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	There are regulatory incentives.	62	6
201407	164	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	Clearly, the incentive—not in the branches here, but for the other parts of a foreign banking organization—to reduce their balance sheet in the most recent quarter were quite strong because of their trying to calculate the $50 billion asset threshold for the IHC requirement.	62	6
201407	165	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	I think it is worthy of more investigation.	62	6
201407	166	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	But overall this is reasonably neutral.	62	6
201407	167	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	I think going in and out, there is no friction within money markets from the existence of the overnight RRP.	62	6
201407	168	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	It probably does make it a little bit easier for some of the people who want to do this behavior to maintain the relationships they have after that.	62	6
201407	169	2014-07-30	meeting	POTTER	If I’m a money fund, I feel less disturbed by the fact that I have to go to the ON RRP for one day, and then I form my relationship back with a foreign banking organization.	62	6

201407	254	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	Let me just make a couple of introductory comments to start things off.	92	9
201407	255	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	I want to begin by once again expressing my appreciation to all of you for the productive discussions you have had over the past two meetings and also for your thoughtful and constructive comments on the draft normalization principles and the memos that were circulated for discussion today.	92	9
201407	256	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	I also want to thank the staff for their continued excellent support.	92	9
201407	257	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	I think we all agree on the importance of clearly communicating to the public our normalization plans well before the first steps in tightening policy become appropriate.	92	9
201407	258	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	In light of the good progress we have made so far, I believe we are on track to roll out our revised policy normalization principles and strategy in September.	92	9
201407	259	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	As you know, staff circulated a revised set of normalization principles yesterday that reflect the comments we received late last week.	92	9
201407	260	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	I hope that any further revisions that seem necessary can be locked down in the coming weeks so that we can finalize and release these principles in September.	92	9
201407	261	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	Therefore, my first goal for today’s meeting is to make sure we agree on the general approach to conducting monetary policy during normalization that is spelled out in the main memo, and incorporated in the policy principles, and that we iron out any remaining issues with the overall approach during today’s session.	92	9
201407	262	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	Secondly, I hope we can make progress on the mechanics of our approach, and in particular on the role and design of the overnight RRP facility, something that is clearly a concern to many of you and to me as well.	92	9
201407	263	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	I think that most of you agree that the overnight RRP facility needs to play a supplementary role in enhancing our control over the federal funds rate during the normalization process.	92	9
201407	264	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	Personally, I will say that I think it’s important for us to demonstrate convincing control over short-term rates at liftoff.	92	9
201407	265	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	But because of our concerns about this facility’s potential to create systemic risk or to cause significant and unintended changes in the structure of money markets, we will definitely need to address these concerns.	92	9
201407	266	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	With respect to the numerical parameters pertaining to the caps, I would suggest that we still have time to work out these details, and we can and should wait to finalize these choices until we have done some further testing.	92	9
201407	267	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	We are likely, in that testing process, to learn more about usage and the limits that will be needed to establish adequate monetary control.	92	9
201407	268	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	There is no need to nail down the parameters today.	92	9
201407	269	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	That said, I will surely be asked questions about the facility in September, and I’d like to be able to describe some of the key design features of the overnight RRP facility at the press conference.	92	9
201407	270	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	But the draft normalization principles omit technical details, and I think we can say at that time that we have made no final decisions on numerical parameters.	92	9
201407	271	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	A third goal today is to address how we will handle intermeeting adjustments in the event that the funds rate moves outside the target range set by the Committee.	92	9
201407	272	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	As we have discussed before, under the unprecedented circumstances we face, we cannot know with certainty how well any specific approach to normalization will work in practice.	92	9
201407	273	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	We, thus, need to be able to adjust our mix of tools flexibly.	92	9
201407	274	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	One important issue raised in the staff memos regards the possible need to make an adjustment to one of our tools between FOMC meetings in order to help keep the funds rate in the Committee’s target range.	92	9
201407	275	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	We hope that this need would not arise very often, but I think we need arrangements for making adjustments that are prompt and effective and also appropriate from a governance standpoint.	92	9
201407	276	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	As noted in the staff memos, one possibility is for the Committee, at the outset, to delegate carefully circumscribed authority to me as Chair to make such intermeeting adjustments.	92	9
201407	277	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	I want to make clear that I am not asking for this authority now, but I am interested in hearing your views on how we should proceed if, say, the federal funds rate moves significantly or persistently outside of our target range.	92	9
201407	278	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	Of course, the Committee is responsible for setting the stance of monetary policy, and I would not support any plan that, in practice or in appearance, distances the Committee from policy decisions.	92	9

201407	282	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	With that, I am going to turn the floor over to Patrick McCabe, who is going to start us off on the staff presentation.	92	9
201407	283	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201407	284	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	My colleagues and I will be referring to the exhibits labeled “Monetary Policy Normalization.”	92	9
201407	285	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	At the June FOMC meeting, many of you emphasized that using an ON RRP facility during the normalization process could have unintended effects on financial markets.	92	9
201407	286	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Participants noted the possibility that surges in take-up during periods of financial stress could exacerbate dislocations in funding markets and that expanding the Federal Reserve’s footprint in financial intermediation could reshape markets in unpredictable ways that could prove undesirable.	92	9
201407	287	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	However, the Committee has also recognized over the past several months the potential utility of an ON RRP facility.	92	9
201407	288	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	In particular, it was generally agreed that the facility could play an important supporting role for IOER by helping to put a firmer floor under money market rates when the time comes to tighten policy.	92	9
201407	289	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Thus, the risks on which the Committee focused in June need to be weighed against the usefulness of an ON RRP facility in improving control over the federal funds rate during normalization.	92	9
201407	290	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Given this tradeoff, participants discussed several design features—including constraints on usage and a relatively wide spread between the ON RRP and IOER rates—that could help address unintended consequences while preserving the usefulness of the facility for implementing monetary policy.	92	9
201407	291	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	In that discussion, participants appeared to envision an ON RRP facility that would be relatively small and limited in its possible growth, which would provide opportunities for adjustment by the Committee as experience is gained, and that would not remain in place permanently.	92	9
201407	292	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	In my remarks, I will discuss a specific structure for an ON RRP facility that has these features.	92	9
201407	293	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	This proposal, which aims to address participants’ concerns while maintaining the facility’s ability to assist in managing the level of short-term rates, was the subject of one of the memos that you received in advance of this meeting.	92	9
201407	294	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	The top-left panel of exhibit 1 outlines the basic structure of the staff proposal and its key parameters.	92	9
201407	295	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Clearly, the Committee could choose a different configuration of these parameters, and the initial settings could be adjusted during the normalization process, as experience and the Committee’s weighing of considerations dictate.	92	9
201407	296	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	First, reflecting the Committee’s concerns about the potential size of the program in normal times, the spread between the ON RRP rate and the IOER rate would be 25 basis points, a bit wider than the current spread.	92	9
201407	297	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Second, the proposal includes two distinct safeguards that are intended to mitigate the possible adverse effects discussed by participants in June—that is, usage would be the lesser of:  (1) a $500 billion overall limit on the size of the program that is intended to place a bound on the Federal Reserve’s footprint in money markets, and (2) a dynamic aggregate circuit-breaker cap that aims to limit sudden and potentially disruptive surges in take-up that may occur in periods of financial stress.	92	9
201407	298	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	As outlined in the memo, the circuit-breaker cap would be equal to average usage over the previous five business days plus $100 billion.	92	9
201407	299	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	We expect take-up at the facility to remain below the overall limit in normal times, particularly given the wide spread between the ON RRP and IOER rates.	92	9
201407	300	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	In the event that the circuit-breaker cap reached the overall limit, the Desk would consult with the Committee regarding possible policy responses.	92	9
201407	301	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	The Committee could also delegate to the Chair the authority to make limited, temporary changes to the overall limit or circuit-breaker cap during an intermeeting period.	92	9
201407	302	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Finally, the cap system would be implemented as part of a daily uniform-rate auction, which would provide a market-based allocation mechanism that sets the rate on ON RRPs in the event that either of the caps is binding.	92	9
201407	303	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	That auction could also have limits on the take-up by any single counterparty to preserve broad access to the facility and discourage counterparty business models that may depend on large potential use of ON RRP.	92	9
201407	304	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	As noted to the right, the combination of the overall limit on usage and the circuit- breaker cap has some advantages over either safeguard on its own.	92	9
201407	305	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	An overall limit on aggregate take-up assures that the Committee would determine the maximum size of the facility.	92	9
201407	306	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	A circuit-breaker cap alone would constrain surges on a given day but would not prevent take-up from continuing to rise over time.	92	9
201407	307	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	To be sure, an overall limit on its own would be more straightforward and likely simpler to communicate to the public.	92	9
201407	308	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	However, it could allow very large surges into the facility when recent usage has been low, unless the overall limit itself is very low, but a very low limit might bind often and materially reduce the facility’s ability to establish a floor on short-term rates.	92	9
201407	309	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	The circuit-breaker cap, in contrast, could be effective in containing surges without binding frequently.	92	9
201407	310	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Another advantage of including a circuit-breaker cap is that its automatic adjustments in response to routine market developments would not convey information about policy intent.	92	9
201407	311	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	The middle panel illustrates the proposed combination of safeguards using actual ON RRP usage to date—that is, the gray bars in the panel.	92	9
201407	312	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	To be sure, if the current exercise, which employs uniform caps for each counterparty, is modified to utilize the proposal’s combination of aggregate caps, future counterparty behavior and take-up may differ from current patterns.	92	9
201407	313	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Still, observed take-up provides a useful means of illustrating the relative utility of different types of aggregate caps.	92	9
201407	314	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	The blue line shows the proposed circuit-breaker cap.	92	9
201407	315	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Beginning on January 30, when the authorization of the exercise was extended for one year, that circuit-breaker cap would have been binding just twice, on the quarter-end dates of March 31 and June 30.	92	9
201407	316	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Potential one-day surges into the facility—that is, the differences between the heights of the bars and the blue line—would have averaged $98 billion, with a standard deviation of $26 billion and a maximum of $145 billion.	92	9
201407	317	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	In contrast, a standalone $500 billion overall limit, the red dashed line, would never have been binding to date, but it would have allowed very large surges into the facility.	92	9
201407	318	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	The average potential surge with such a static cap on its own would have been $378 billion over the sample period, and the maximum potential surge, $451 billion.	92	9
201407	319	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	The proposed circuit-breaker cap, as mentioned earlier, would be based on average usage over the previous 5 business days.	92	9
201407	320	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	As discussed in the appendix of the staff memo, the 5-day moving average has some advantages over alternative measures, such as average usage over the previous month, calendar week, and 10 business days.	92	9
201407	321	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Compared with caps set using these alternative measures and calibrated to allow similar magnitudes of average potential surge, a cap based on a 5-day moving average would have been binding or close to binding on fewer days.	92	9
201407	322	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Moreover, because of its greater sensitivity to changing conditions, this cap would have resulted in lower volatility in potential one-day surges and a smaller maximum potential surge.	92	9
201407	323	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Measuring previous usage over a longer period would make the cap less responsive to evolving market conditions and would result in greater variation in potential surges into the facility.	92	9
201407	324	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	That said, during a period of financial stress, a cap based on a shorter period, such as the proposed 5-day moving average, could increase fairly quickly.	92	9
201407	325	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Such a cap itself could rise by more than $100 billion in a week and allow for larger potential surges into the facility.	92	9
201407	326	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	This point highlights that this type of cap should be considered primarily as a circuit breaker intended to limit the size of an initial surge while giving the Committee a few days to assess the situation and consider policy alternatives.	92	9
201407	327	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	The lower-left panel highlights some key remaining questions for the Committee.	92	9
201407	328	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	First, is the proposed structure of the facility, including the combination of an overall limit on the size of the program and a circuit-breaker cap, appropriate?	92	9
201407	329	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Second, if so, are the proposed calibrations appropriate?	92	9
201407	330	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Is $500 billion the right level for the overall limit?	92	9
201407	331	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Is $100 billion the right amount to add to past usage to set the circuit- breaker cap?	92	9
201407	332	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Should past usage be based on the average take-up over the previous five business days?	92	9
201407	333	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Of course, if the proposal were adopted—with these calibrations or with others—the parameters could always be adjusted as more is learned about the operations, effectiveness, and usefulness of the program.	92	9
201407	334	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	A related question is whether to allow the circuit-breaker cap to bind occasionally, such as at quarter-ends.	92	9
201407	335	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Doing so would allow staff and market participants to become more familiar with the operational procedures associated with a binding cap, such as the auction process, so that their first experience with a binding cap would not occur during a period of market stress.	92	9
201407	336	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Furthermore, having caps that bind occasionally would encourage market participants to temper their reliance on the ON RRP facility and better incorporate in their contingency planning the possibility that an auction may leave them with more uninvested cash than expected late in the day.	92	9
201407	337	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	A potential cost is the reduction in the facility’s effectiveness in establishing a floor on rates, directly on the days when the caps bind and perhaps also indirectly as counterparties adjust their strategies in response to the expectation that the caps will bind occasionally.	92	9
201407	338	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Regarding timing and communications, as noted to the right, the Committee could adopt the proposed combination of an overall limit and a circuit-breaker cap with a new resolution authorizing the ON RRP exercise at the September meeting.	92	9
201407	339	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	The Committee also could publicize the shift to a new structure in conjunction with the announcement of the normalization principles and through a Desk statement.	92	9
201407	340	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	The authorization might also include options for additional testing of the design features of this proposal, particularly given the remaining uncertainties about the efficacy of the proposal in establishing a floor on short-term rates.	92	9
201407	341	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	The results of these tests could inform the Committee’s balancing of its objectives of managing the level of short-term rates and mitigating concerns about financial-stability risks, and aid in refining its calibration of key parameters.	92	9
201407	342	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	The Committee might also consider small-value tests of a binding cap outside of the regular daily operations.	92	9
201407	343	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Such tests could provide some operational experience with a binding cap while limiting any effect on interest rate control.	92	9
201407	344	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	In addition, during the testing process, staff could consider whether the use of projections for normal ON RRP demand would be more effective for setting the circuit-breaker cap than measures of past usage.	92	9
201407	345	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	If projections were used in this manner, the Desk could publish in advance its projections for take-up and the resulting levels of the cap.	92	9
201407	346	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	If the Committee is interested in testing any of the design features of the facility, including those that I have highlighted or others, the staff could provide a more specific proposal for testing for approval by the Committee.	92	9
201407	347	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Such a proposal also would outline how to assess the test results in terms of costs and benefits and the tradeoff between the two objectives of managing the level of short-term interest rates and mitigating financial-stability risks.	92	9
201407	348	2014-07-30	meeting	McCABE	Gretchen will now continue our briefing.	92	9
201407	349	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	Thank you, Patrick.	92	9
201407	350	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	In my remarks, I will summarize the key aspects of the overall approach to normalization discussed in the staff memo, and then describe some possible adjustments that could be made to allow for a smaller role for the overnight RRP facility if that were desired.	92	9
201407	351	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	As noted in the top panel of your second exhibit, under the approach in the staff memo, you would continue to set a target range of 25 basis points for the federal funds rate; that target range would be your primary means of communicating the stance of monetary policy.	92	9
201407	352	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	Framing the stance of policy in terms of the federal funds rate would focus monetary policy discussions and communication on a rate that is familiar to market participants and the public.	92	9
201407	353	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	In addition, setting a target range rather than a point target would afford some leeway in achieving your stated interest rate policy while the quantity of reserves in the banking system remains elevated, and could be especially helpful during the early stages of liftoff.	92	9
201407	354	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	The IOER and overnight RRP rates would be used as tools to move the effective federal funds rate into the target range and to maintain it within that range.	92	9
201407	355	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	The IOER rate would be set equal to the top of the target range and the overnight RRP rate set equal to the bottom of the target range, settings that would be straightforward to communicate.	92	9
201407	356	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	Because the resulting spread of 25 basis points would be a little wider than the current 20 basis points, it should continue to encourage a volume of trading in the federal funds market that is similar to the current level.	92	9
201407	357	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	A spread of 25 basis points would also help to mitigate concerns about having a large footprint in the nonbank financial sector during normal times.	92	9
201407	358	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	As I already noted, I’ll return to the topic of the role of overnight RRP operations in this approach a bit later.	92	9
201407	359	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	Communicating adjustments to the stance of policy would be straightforward under this approach.	92	9
201407	360	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	For example, the first tightening move could be to set the target range to 25 to 50 basis points, with the IOER rate at 50 basis points and the overnight RRP rate at 25 basis points.	92	9
201407	361	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	Subsequently, the target range could be adjusted in steps of 25 basis points, or multiples thereof.	92	9
201407	362	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	At a typical FOMC meeting, you would primarily focus on setting the target range for the federal funds rate.	92	9
201407	363	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	The staff memo included an illustrative draft of a postmeeting liftoff statement announcing the first change in the target range.	92	9
201407	364	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	The statement notes that, “In a related action to help move the effective federal funds rate into the new target range,” the Board had changed the IOER rate.	92	9
201407	365	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	It also notes that the Board had approved a change in the primary credit rate in the same way that changes in the discount rate have been communicated for quite some time.	92	9
201407	366	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	Next, the draft statement also notes that the FOMC had changed the overnight RRP rate.	92	9
201407	367	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	Mentioning the IOER rate first in the statement, and the overnight RRP rate subsequently, would help to signal that the IOER rate was seen as playing the primary role in implementing monetary policy.	92	9
201407	368	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	Of course, you do not have to mention the overnight RRP rate in your statement; it could be noted in the directive to the Desk instead.	92	9
201407	369	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	Assuming that the limits on usage of overnight RRPs were designed to rarely bind, as presumed in the staff memo, the staff expects that this approach would result in the effective federal funds rate residing in the lower portion of the target range.	92	9
201407	370	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	But if the federal funds rate were to move outside of its target range, you might find that you need to adjust some of the parameters of this approach, or employ other measures.	92	9
201407	371	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	As noted in the bottom-left panel, your preferred response would likely depend on the specific circumstances at hand.	92	9
201407	372	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	For example, if the baseline approach works broadly as intended, but the effective federal funds rate nonetheless moved out of its target range often enough and by a sufficient amount to warrant a response of some sort, you might decide to adjust the administered rates.	92	9
201407	373	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	Such adjustments could be made at the next scheduled FOMC meeting, or you might prefer to hold an unscheduled joint meeting of the Committee and Board.	92	9
201407	374	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	Alternatively, the Board and FOMC may want to delegate to the Chair the authority to make modest adjustments to the IOER and overnight RRP rates between meetings, if such changes were judged necessary to keep the effective federal funds rate within the target range established by the FOMC.	92	9
201407	375	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	For the same reason, as Patrick noted, you might also choose to authorize the Chair to adjust the caps on usage of the overnight RRP facility, if necessary.	92	9
201407	376	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	The Board and Committee would, of course, set limits on the size of the adjustments that the Chair could make under delegated authority and, consistent with past practice, the Board and Committee could instruct the Chair to consult them, if feasible, before making any intermeeting adjustments.	92	9
201407	377	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	If such adjustments were not successful in keeping the funds rate in its target range, there are several additional steps that you could take if warranted.	92	9
201407	378	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	For example, if the federal funds rate remained persistently below the bottom of its target range, you could use term-draining tools or sales of short-term Treasury securities to firm money market conditions.	92	9
201407	379	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	You may want to consider ways to alter this approach in order to allow for a more complete assessment of the need for overnight RRP operations as part of the normalization strategy, as noted in the bottom-right panel.	92	9
201407	380	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	One possibility would be to lift off by setting the target range for the federal funds rate to 25 to 50 basis points and the IOER rate to the top of that range, just as in the baseline approach, but keep the overnight RRP rate at its current level of 5 basis points.	92	9
201407	381	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	Relative to the baseline approach, having a wider spread between the IOER and overnight RRP rates at the outset should reduce the attractiveness of the facility, but it would also result in the facility providing a lower floor on short-term interest rates.	92	9
201407	382	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	It is possible that the federal funds rate and other short-term interest rates could move up nearly one for one with increases in the IOER rate.	92	9
201407	383	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	If so, the Committee could subsequently maintain the wider spread between the IOER and overnight RRP rates, or consider widening that spread further in order to minimize use of the overnight RRP facility.	92	9
201407	384	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	However, if the IOER rate did not provide enough lift for the federal funds rate or other short- term rates, the Committee would likely need to make adjustments to the overnight RRP rate to move the funds rate into the target range.	92	9
201407	385	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	But in this case the first policy tightening would not have been successful, which could significantly undermine the Federal Reserve’s credibility and greatly increase uncertainty in financial markets.	92	9
201407	386	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	Such an outcome could also have reputational consequences in the political sphere, in which criticism of the asset purchase programs has included concerns about difficulty of exit.	92	9
201407	387	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	As a consequence, the Committee might want to take a more cautious course by first using the approach in the staff memo to lift off from the effective zero lower bound, setting the target range for the federal funds rate to 25 to 50 basis points and the IOER and overnight RRP rates to the top and bottom of that range, respectively.	92	9
201407	388	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	From that policy position, the Committee could then assess the size of the overnight RRP facility and conditions in money markets, and decide if the spread between the overnight RRP and IOER rates could be widened while still maintaining acceptable control over the level of the federal funds rate and other short-term rates.	92	9
201407	389	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	When it seemed prudent, the Committee could widen that spread, either at the time of the next policy tightening or sooner if desired.	92	9
201407	390	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	Such an approach would be consistent with the Committee learning about the tools during normalization and making adjustments to their use in order to best balance the Committee’s various objectives.	92	9
201407	391	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	That said, assessing the contribution of the overnight RRP facility to the behavior of the federal funds rate, a key feature of this approach, could be difficult.	92	9
201407	392	2014-07-30	meeting	WEINBACH	Steve will now continue our briefing.	92	9

201407	404	2014-07-30	meeting	MEYER	Exhibit 4 shows the principles as major bullets and the Committee’s current thinking, as we understand it, about how it will implement each principle in indented subbullets.	92	9
201407	405	2014-07-30	meeting	MEYER	Exhibit 5 more sharply separates tactics from principles.	92	9
201407	406	2014-07-30	meeting	MEYER	The key differences in the draft normalization principles shown in exhibits 4 and 5, from the June 2011 exit principles, include:  (1) ceasing or reducing reinvestments will come after the first increase in the federal funds rate, rather than before; (2) instead of referring to “temporary reserve-draining operations,” as in 2011, the current drafts refer to temporary use of an overnight RRP facility and other supplementary tools; and (3) the Committee now anticipates that it will rely primarily on ending reinvestments rather than on selling assets to reduce its securities holdings—particularly its holdings of MBS—although it retains the option to sell MBS to eliminate residual holdings in the longer run.	92	9
201407	407	2014-07-30	meeting	MEYER	The strikeouts and red text in exhibit 4 show the changes from the draft that we sent you with the memos on July 18.	92	9
201407	408	2014-07-30	meeting	MEYER	With respect to the high-level principles, the key change is adding back language, in the fourth principle, that explains why the Committee intends to reduce its securities holdings and return to holding primarily Treasury securities.	92	9
201407	409	2014-07-30	meeting	MEYER	With respect to tactics, there are two major changes from the earlier version.	92	9
201407	410	2014-07-30	meeting	MEYER	The first is to make clear that a standing ON RRP facility will be a supplementary tool to be used only as necessary to help improve control over the federal funds rate and, further, that the facility will be phased out as soon as it is no longer needed for this purpose.	92	9
201407	411	2014-07-30	meeting	MEYER	The second major change is to state that the Committee “currently anticipates that it will normalize the size and composition of its portfolio primarily by ceasing to reinvest repayments of principal on securities held in the System Open Market Account.”	92	9
201407	412	2014-07-30	meeting	MEYER	These words indicate that the Committee expects to let maturing Treasuries roll off but does not expect to sell Treasury securities.	92	9
201407	413	2014-07-30	meeting	MEYER	However, other new language—language stating that, during normalization, the Federal Reserve will use “other supplementary tools as needed to help improve control over the federal funds rate”	92	9
201407	414	2014-07-30	meeting	MEYER	—holds open the possibility of selling either Treasury securities or MBS if necessary to maintain control of the funds rate.	92	9
201407	415	2014-07-30	meeting	MEYER	The changes that I just summarized are also incorporated in exhibit 5, though they are not shown in strikeout and red in that exhibit.	92	9

201407	1001	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	First on my list is President Rosengren.	92	9
201407	1002	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201407	1003	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	I support the general approach in the revised principles and strategies of normalization.	92	9
201407	1004	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	I’d also prefer the reorganized revised principles, though I do have a few suggestions.	92	9
201407	1005	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	First, I view the use of the federal funds rate as a communication tool rather than a hard target.	92	9
201407	1006	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	This is consistent with the second main bullet in the reorganized revised principles memo that says, “The Committee intends to adjust the stance of monetary policy primarily through actions that influence the level of the federal funds rate and other short-term rates.”	92	9
201407	1007	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	I like that phrasing.	92	9
201407	1008	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	“Influence” is not the same as “target.”	92	9
201407	1009	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Specifically, we are communicating using a federal funds range, but it is important to move short-term rates more generally.	92	9
201407	1010	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	I am less concerned about a thinly traded market dominated by the GSEs.	92	9
201407	1011	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	I would like some more background provided at future meetings on federal funds trading patterns to get a better understanding of the arbitrage relative to IOER, as President Lockhart had suggested.	92	9
201407	1012	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Second, I like the principles document having no numbers.	92	9
201407	1013	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Precise numbers have a way of becoming hardwired and difficult to change.	92	9
201407	1014	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	I would prefer that we not hardwire details until we are more confident about how markets will react to our actions and gain experience that can help us better understand the interrelationships among the IOER, the overnight reverse repo facility, and the federal funds rate.	92	9
201407	1015	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Given the concerns raised about the overnight reverse repo facility, it may be worth making a technical change that would help us infer how much we can rely on the IOER alone.	92	9
201407	1016	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	I would suggest that we make a technical adjustment to the IOER of perhaps 5 or 10 basis points at a meeting prior to when we officially begin to tighten policy.	92	9
201407	1017	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	If all relevant short-term rates move up, we can have more confidence that we can more heavily rely on IOER as our policy instrument.	92	9
201407	1018	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	I would also note that I would view it as a significant problem if we observed little response by other relevant short-term rates through an announcement that we were tightening policy by 25 basis points using only the IOER.	92	9
201407	1019	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	We have said in speeches and testimony that we are confident that we can raise rates when that becomes appropriate.	92	9
201407	1020	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Announcing our intention to raise short-term rates with only modest reactions from short rates other than our administered rate would seriously harm our credibility and could lead to unnecessary financial turbulence.	92	9
201407	1021	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	We need to carefully balance the goal of meeting our monetary policy objectives with the legitimate concerns raised about the reverse repo facility.	92	9
201407	1022	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	I would view the initial announcement to tighten as critical to meet our monetary policy objectives.	92	9
201407	1023	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Depending on the market reaction, I would then adjust the reverse repo facility and potentially the IOER−ON RRP rate spread.	92	9
201407	1024	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	In terms of the caps, I would eliminate the dynamic aggregate circuit breaker.	92	9
201407	1025	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	The two main concerns raised at the previous meeting regarding the reverse repo facility were that the facility would have too large a footprint in short-term credit markets, and that the facility would exacerbate financial-stability problems during periods of financial turmoil.	92	9
201407	1026	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Having a large initial spread and an initial overall cap seems sufficient to avoid these two issues.	92	9
201407	1027	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, the dynamic aggregate circuit-breakers do not as effectively address either concern and will be quite complicated to explain.	92	9
201407	1028	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	For example, I am not sure why I should be concerned with declines or surges in the reverse repo facility take-up that have been primarily influenced by end-of-quarter window-dressing, which largely reflects decisions being made by foreign branches.	92	9
201407	1029	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Better understanding the role of foreign branches in short-term credit markets at future meetings would also be useful.	92	9
201407	1030	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	In addition, it is not obvious to me that a $100 billion change in the use of our overnight reverse repo facility constitutes an alarming change in short-term markets or will significantly affect the global supply of short-term credit.	92	9
201407	1031	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Given the size of financial markets, and the fluctuations in the facility to date, the dynamic cap is set quite low and would likely be influenced by one-day declines or surges that seem immaterial as long as the overall cap is not breached.	92	9
201407	1032	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	I would also prefer to keep the caps simple.	92	9
201407	1033	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	A complicated structure may imply more permanence than necessary.	92	9
201407	1034	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	I would imagine an initial cap that would be lowered when it becomes clear that the IOER is sufficient to move short-term market rates when that is appropriate.	92	9
201407	1035	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	The key point is that we need to be confident that we can move short-term market interest rates when that is appropriate.	92	9
201407	1036	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	We can scale the reverse repo facility flexibly as we learn more about how rates react to our actions.	92	9
201407	1037	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	I think the revised principles make clear that this is a temporary facility.	92	9
201407	1038	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Finally, I would not rule out using our balance sheet for financial-stability purposes, which is relevant to President Kocherlakota’s comments.	92	9
201407	1039	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you.	92	9
