201407	1042	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201407	1043	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Thanks to some helpful memos from the staff and from some other Committee participants, I can be relatively brief on the questions on the table today.	92	9
201407	1044	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	There is one important issue I would like to spend a little time on.	92	9
201407	1045	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	I’ll save it for last.	92	9
201407	1046	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	First, I support the general structure of the approach to conducting monetary policy during normalization outlined by the staff, including the directive and the statement.	92	9
201407	1047	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Like President Plosser, I don’t see a need for the proposed delegations of authority to the Chair.	92	9
201407	1048	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	In the past, we have been able to schedule videoconference meetings on very short notice.	92	9
201407	1049	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	And in this instance, the potential need for consultation is fairly predictable, so we might even want to schedule a videoconference in advance for the week after our liftoff announcement.	92	9
201407	1050	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	As for the structure of the overnight reverse repurchase facility, I very much share the concerns expressed eloquently by Governors Tarullo and Powell and President Plosser.	92	9
201407	1051	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	I strongly support their proposal for a significantly lower overall cap.	92	9
201407	1052	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	I agree with President Rosengren; I don’t believe a surge cap is necessary.	92	9
201407	1053	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	It’s complicated and a bit too fussy.	92	9
201407	1054	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	I also support President Kocherlakota’s proposal to issue a public consultation paper.	92	9
201407	1055	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	The implementation of such a facility is clearly as consequential as many other things that we’ve put out for public comment on the grounds that they have an effect on the industrial organization of a particular sector.	92	9
201407	1056	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	And I think there are useful things we could learn from the process, despite all the research that the Desk has done.	92	9
201407	1057	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Regarding the spread between the IOER and the overnight RRP rates, 25 basis points is about the smallest spread I could support, including the option outlined today by the staff of leaving the interest rate on ON RRPs at 5 basis points when we lift off.	92	9
201407	1058	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	If the RP rate doesn’t rise, we can raise IOER within a week or two and limit the egg-on-the-face phenomenon to a relatively short time horizon.	92	9
201407	1059	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Regarding the spread between the IOER and the discount window rate, the rate on primary credit, I question leaving it at 50 basis points.	92	9
201407	1060	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	We haven’t discussed this at all, and we haven’t seen any staff analysis.	92	9
201407	1061	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	We had a fairly thoroughgoing study when we first set the spread at 100 basis points more than a decade ago.	92	9
201407	1062	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	I think it deserves more thought, and I think the Committee would benefit from staff analysis of the pros and cons of a spread of 50 basis points versus restoring what I thought we carried around as our view of the normal spread of 100 basis points.	92	9
201407	1063	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	For the most part, I support the new statement of our normalization principles.	92	9
201407	1064	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	I particularly support the revisions to the second bullet point that emphasize the possibility that we could withdraw and wind down the program, and that we intend to use it only as a supplementary tool.	92	9
201407	1065	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Finally, I would like to make a few observations about the plans for our holdings of the securities issued by or backed by Fannie Mae and Freddie Mac.	92	9
201407	1066	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	There is a tension within the principles as written, and President Plosser raised this question during a Q&A.	92	9
201407	1067	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	In one sub-bullet we state that we don’t intend to sell Fannie Mae and Freddie Mac securities.	92	9
201407	1068	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	In the second-to- last bullet, we say we want to minimize the effect of reserve holdings on the allocation of credit across sectors of the economy.	92	9
201407	1069	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	And these two, I think, directly conflict.	92	9
201407	1070	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	If we want to minimize credit allocation, we would obviously plan to sell Fannie Mae and Freddie Mac securities as soon as possible.	92	9
201407	1071	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	You might be wondering what credit allocation looks like.	92	9
201407	1072	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Fortunately, the staff has provided us with quantitative estimates of the effects.	92	9
201407	1073	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	An August 28, 2012, memo reports the estimates of the effects of buying $500 billion of long-term US Treasury securities and compares that with the effects of buying $500 billion in MBS.	92	9
201407	1074	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Buying Treasuries is estimated to lower both mortgage rates and the Treasury term premium by the same amount, 21 basis points.	92	9
201407	1075	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Buying MBS is estimated to lower mortgage rates by more, as you’d expect, 24 basis points, but to lower the term premium by less, only 16 basis points.	92	9
201407	1076	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Combining these estimates implies that by holding MBS rather than Treasuries, we are lowering mortgage rates but raising the term premium on long-term Treasury securities.	92	9
201407	1077	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	For example, if we sold all of our $1.7 trillion in MBS and bought Treasuries with the proceeds, the theoretical effect would be to raise mortgage rates by 10 basis points, but to lower the Treasury term premium by 17 basis points.	92	9
201407	1078	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	And we have been operating on the notion that the Treasury term premium passes through to other people’s borrowing rates, so borrowers outside the housing market are, in essence, paying higher interest rates by 17 basis points as a result of us choosing to hold Fannie Mae and Freddie Mac securities instead of US Treasuries.	92	9
201407	1079	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Now, there may be reasons for variance.	92	9
201407	1080	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Actual results may not match up with the staff’s estimate, but—	92	9
201407	1081	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	Don’t try this at home.	92	9
201407	1082	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	[Laughter]	92	9
201407	1083	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	And the staff may have updated the rest of this, but these are the estimates on which we based our decisionmaking in September 2012, when we embarked on the latest purchase program.	92	9
201407	1084	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	I think they’re the best we have to go on regarding this effect.	92	9
201407	1085	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	So this is a measure, a 27 basis point twist in relative borrowing rates, that we’re engineering by holding MBS instead of Treasuries alone.	92	9
201407	1086	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Now, you might be tempted to resolve this tension by deleting the clause about minimizing credit allocation, but that’s not the only source of tension.	92	9
201407	1087	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	For several decades now the Committee has had standing guidelines for the conduct of System open market operations in federal agency issues.	92	9
201407	1088	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	They state that “System open market operations in federal agency issues are not designed to support individual sectors of the market or to channel funds into issues of particular agencies.”	92	9
201407	1089	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Now, it’s true that these guidelines were temporarily suspended in January 2009, but we did not abolish them, and they’re still on the Board’s website.	92	9
201407	1090	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Moreover, these guidelines have deep roots in Federal Reserve history.	92	9
201407	1091	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	They were first adopted in August 1971, a few years after Congress passed legislation authorizing Federal Reserve purchases of federal agency securities.	92	9
201407	1092	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	They did that with the intent to allow the Fed to buy the obligations of Fannie Mae and Federal Home Loan Banks to support the housing market.	92	9
201407	1093	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	The Board did not want to buy agency securities, and the FOMC initially instructed the Desk to just test doing repos in agency securities but to hold off making outright purchases.	92	9
201407	1094	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	But Congress repeatedly pressured the Fed to use its authority to make outright purchases and had some very contentious hearings on the subject.	92	9
201407	1095	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Senator Proxmire explicitly threatened legislation to reduce the Fed’s independence.	92	9
201407	1096	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	For a time the Fed resisted.	92	9
201407	1097	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Chairman William McChesney Martin testified that to have any effect on mortgage rates, the Fed would necessarily have to restrict credit to other sectors of the economy, such as state and local governments and business borrowers, consistent with our staff’s 2012 estimate.	92	9
201407	1098	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	He said that it would “violate a fundamental principle of sound monetary policy in that it would attempt to use credit-creating powers of the Central Bank to subsidize programs benefiting special sectors of the economy.”	92	9
201407	1099	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Arthur Burns wrote in a similar context, “Decisions as to social priorities in the use of credit are inherently political in character.	92	9
201407	1100	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	If such decisions are to be made at all, they should be made by the Congress, not by an administrative and nonpolitical body such as the Federal Reserve.	92	9
201407	1101	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	After all, tilting credit in favor of some borrowers implies denying credit to someone else.”	92	9
201407	1102	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	The most problematic source of tension surrounding our MBS holdings, however, is the March 2009 joint statement by the Department of Treasury and the Federal Reserve, titled “The Role of the Federal Reserve in Preserving Financial and Monetary Stability.”	92	9
201407	1103	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	The second point in that document states, “Actions taken by the Federal Reserve should also aim to improve financial or credit conditions broadly, not to allocate credit to narrowly defined sectors or classes of borrowers.	92	9
201407	1104	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Government decisions to influence the allocation of credit are the province of fiscal authorities.”	92	9
201407	1105	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	So here we are, quite clearly engaged in credit allocation.	92	9
201407	1106	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Our holdings of Fannie and Freddie securities are lowering mortgage rates by 10 basis points and raising borrowing costs outside the home mortgage arena by 17 basis points, and yet the official policy of the Federal Reserve and the Treasury is that influencing the allocation of credit is the province of fiscal authorities and not the Federal Reserve.	92	9
201407	1107	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	I don’t see how to reconcile these two.	92	9
201407	1108	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	I don’t see how we can justify deciding on our very own that more housing activity and less business investment would be a good thing.	92	9
201407	1109	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	I don’t think we can claim we are ameliorating a dysfunctional market for mortgage-backed securities, as we might have plausibly claimed at the end of 2008.	92	9
201407	1110	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	I don’t see us arguing that we should hold onto Fannie and Freddie securities to avoid realizing capital losses and impairing our remittances to Treasury.	92	9
201407	1111	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	I also don’t see how to ignore the political risks associated with continuing to hold Fannie and Freddie securities indefinitely.	92	9
201407	1112	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	The longer we hold them, the longer the door is open to what I think are mischievous efforts to involve us more deeply or permanently in housing finance.	92	9
201407	1113	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	GSE legislation came close to passing in the Senate earlier this year, and it failed because of an apparent inability to bridge the gap between the desire of affordable housing advocates for more resources and the desire of others to limit the resources extracted from the housing finance sector for that purpose.	92	9
201407	1114	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	It seems plausible to me that some bright minds on the Hill will turn to the Fed’s balance sheet to attempt to bridge that gap.	92	9
201407	1115	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	After all, our balance sheet has been raided in the past to provide ersatz solutions to fiscal problems.	92	9
201407	1116	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	So I continue to believe it’s a mistake for us to buy and hold securities issued by or backed by Fannie Mae or Freddie Mac.	92	9
201407	1117	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	I recognize I may be out of step with the brave new world of central bank activism.	92	9
201407	1118	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	I recognize that our long journey into housing finance is less troublesome to many of the participants in this Committee, but from a broader historical perspective, this strikes me as an important component of our deliberations today, one that deserves careful thought.	92	9
201407	1119	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Should we continue along the path we seem to be on, of holding Fannie and Freddie securities to maturity, I believe some public explanation of our stance on credit allocation is necessary.	92	9
201407	1120	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9

201407	1122	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Powell.	92	9
201407	1123	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201407	1124	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	In case it proves controversial later, I’d like to start by saying at the outset that I agree with the Chair that it’s unwise and premature to try to make a firm decision today on the precise numerical parameters of the facility.	92	9
201407	1125	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	At the September meeting the Chair can set forth the draft normalization principles that we finalize and release.	92	9
201407	1126	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	She can discuss them at the press conference.	92	9
201407	1127	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	She can describe the facility as narrow in purpose, scope, and time.	92	9
201407	1128	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	She can say that there will be appropriate size limitations in place, including aggregate and surge caps if appropriate, and that in finalizing those restrictions before liftoff, we’re all going to be informed by testing results and use patterns that we observe and analyze over the coming months.	92	9
201407	1129	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	So just to underscore that point.	92	9
201407	1130	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	If you ignore the quarter ends and look at the use patterns so far, we had a spike in April and May to the $200 billion range, really because of cash flow coming into Treasury and, therefore, bill supply decline.	92	9
201407	1131	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	Other than that, usage has been in the $100 billion to $150 billion range.	92	9
201407	1132	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	And maybe those levels will rise between now and liftoff.	92	9
201407	1133	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	We don’t know that.	92	9
201407	1134	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	But if we try to make a decision today, it stands a big chance of being off by quite a bit, and therefore, the incentive is to guess high so as to avoid weakening monetary control—for example, by having a $500 billion overall cap, which is so much higher than these other levels.	92	9
201407	1135	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	By next spring or summer when it’s time for liftoff, the Committee will have a much longer period of data that’s been observed when we are trying to set these levels.	92	9
201407	1136	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	Let me turn to the four questions in the appendix to the memo that we’re asked to respond to.	92	9
201407	1137	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	On the first one, I do support the approach to conducting monetary policy during normalization that is described in the memo, and I would also favor giving the Chair limited discretion to make adjustments to IOER and ON RRP rates in order to keep the federal funds rate within the range set by the FOMC.	92	9
201407	1138	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	I am a little less enthusiastic about giving the Chair intermeeting discretion to increase the aggregate or surge caps, as that would risk sending a signal that the facility is designed to expand; I guess I would support that discretion, but prefer that it be used only as necessary.	92	9
201407	1139	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	Second, I find the draft postmeeting statement broadly acceptable for governing and communicating policy during normalization.	92	9
201407	1140	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	And, third, I also support the draft set of normalization principles set forth as appendix 3, and I think the level and specificity of information are about right.	92	9
201407	1141	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	I am also okay with the alternative version, which divides into principles and tactics.	92	9
201407	1142	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	Coming back to the overnight RRP just for a moment, I support its overall design but have suggested a number of changes, which are set forth in the comments that Governor Tarullo and I submitted before the meeting.	92	9
201407	1143	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	I see the ON RRP exclusively as a monetary policy tool to be deployed as long as needed to provide a floor for the target range for the federal funds rate.	92	9
201407	1144	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	I like the 25 basis point range.	92	9
201407	1145	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	That makes sense to me as an appropriate level of control, and while it might be okay to tolerate a little deviation from that, I would tend to want to see it in that range.	92	9
201407	1146	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	Without going through the whole memo, let me just say that the facility raises serious financial-stability concerns and related concerns about unpredictable effects on industry structure.	92	9
201407	1147	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	At the same time, it is very important, in my view, to demonstrate convincing monetary control at the outset, and for me, that would mean I would want the ON RRP to be used at liftoff to help assure control.	92	9
201407	1148	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	I will also say that the sentence that’s been added to the policy normalization principles about phasing out the facility is a very helpful one.	92	9
201407	1149	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	I want to emphasize one aspect of why, to me, the financial-stability problem—and it has been said by many around the table, and I think it’s right, that the caps would come under pressure during a financial stress event.	92	9
201407	1150	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	I do think that’s right.	92	9
201407	1151	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	But it just seems really unlikely to me that that would ever be a good idea.	92	9
201407	1152	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	It’s one thing to offer liquidity in a crisis.	92	9
201407	1153	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	It’s entirely another thing to invite it to come onto our balance sheet.	92	9
201407	1154	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	So any sense in the market that there is a home here at all, that there is capacity that will be enlarged, is itself potentially very, very destabilizing.	92	9
201407	1155	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	And I think that the Committee needs to lean hard, really, against the perception that that could be the case.	92	9
201407	1156	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	I won’t go through all of the details, but again, I would support reducing the caps.	92	9
201407	1157	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	If I had to make these decisions today—and fortunately, we don’t—I would reduce the aggregate cap to $300 billion and reduce the surge cap to $50 billion.	92	9
201407	1158	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	I don’t see any public purpose to be served in facilitating quarter-end window dressing.	92	9
201407	1159	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	I also think there are some benefits in having a cap that does bind with reasonable frequency, although I wouldn’t want it to bind much at the outset as we’re lifting off.	92	9
201407	1160	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	Those benefits would include sending a signal that hitting the cap is not a big stress event.	92	9
201407	1161	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	In addition, it would acquaint market participants with how the mechanics of allocation will work, and it would send a signal that the Committee’s intent is not to seek or accommodate significantly higher levels of demand over time.	92	9
201407	1162	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	I think changing the window from 5 to 10 days would limit the growth in the facility in times of stress without materially changing its operation in ordinary times.	92	9
201407	1163	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	In terms of adding new counterparties, I guess I would prefer to defer that question until the September meeting when we set forth our principles so that we’re sending the clear signal of limited time and scope for the facility.	92	9
201407	1164	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	Finally, I would offer this.	92	9
201407	1165	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	I share many of the same concerns that President Kocherlakota has, but I am skeptical of the idea of engaging in any kind of public consultation process.	92	9
201407	1166	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	I do like the idea of getting input from the public, and that has been ongoing, but not in a formal consultation process.	92	9
201407	1167	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	I do think that the facility as we’re now talking about proposing it, and the language we’re talking about including, would make it much less of a target in any event, but I think this is actually quite a dangerous precedent and a Rubicon that we’re crossing here.	92	9
201407	1168	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	It’s inviting political actors into our business, and I think that the risks of it would outweigh any potential benefits.	92	9
201407	1169	2014-07-30	meeting	POWELL	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9

201407	1235	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	I have a very lengthy statement.	92	9
201407	1236	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201407	1237	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	[Laughter]	92	9
201407	1238	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	I think we actually have made a great deal of progress on these issues over the past few months, and I think we have really benefited from some exceptional help from the memos and the presentations from the Board and the New York staff.	92	9
201407	1239	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	My main point today is to answer the first question that was asked, and that is that I wholeheartedly endorse the outlined normalization approach of communicating the quarter point range for the federal funds rate with the IOER as our primary tool, and the overnight reverse repo facility playing a supplementary role in that.	92	9
201407	1240	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	I think this appropriately balances the pursuits of monetary control, clear communication, and financial stability.	92	9
201407	1241	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	And importantly, the outlined approach does retain quite a bit of flexibility so that we can evolve our framework as we learn along the way.	92	9
201407	1242	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, my answers to the other questions are going to follow from the same general principles that we need to balance monetary control, clear communications, and financial stability while retaining this tactical flexibility.	92	9
201407	1243	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	In terms of question 1.a., I do support giving the Chair authority to make modest intermeeting adjustments during the normalization process, modest changes in the administered rates.	92	9
201407	1244	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	The repo quantity limits are properly viewed as technical adjustments to support achieving the Committee’s desired range for the federal funds rate.	92	9
201407	1245	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Giving the Chair the authority to make such minor adjustments in the transition period is straightforward to communicate and should be widely viewed as dealing with back-office operational issues.	92	9
201407	1246	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	For question 2, the draft statement and directive are excellent models of how to communicate our policy stance and make clear that we are focused on using the familiar federal funds rate to pursue our monetary objectives and using the administered IOER or overnight reverse repo rates to support a desired federal funds rate outcome.	92	9
201407	1247	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	In terms of question 3, I favor the new reorganized, revised potential policy normalization principles and strategy approach that is in exhibit 5 of the handout.	92	9
201407	1248	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	It appropriately focuses on strategy and not on operational details.	92	9
201407	1249	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	I do have a question about what the title should be, given that the title says “Principles and Strategy” while the document says “principles ... and ... tactics.”	92	9
201407	1250	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	But I think it does have the right mix.	92	9
201407	1251	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	It’s the principles and really the strategy, without getting into the specifics of numbers and all of those issues that we can clarify later.	92	9
201407	1252	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	It communicates clearly that our goal is to best achieve our dual mandate, and then lays out a clear strategy of how to accomplish that goal.	92	9
201407	1253	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	And regarding this suggestion to eliminate any reference to the overnight reverse repo facility, that does seem to run counter to our goals of transparency and clarity.	92	9
201407	1254	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	The statement already makes clear—and the revised statement, I think, does a good job of this—it makes clear that the repo facility is in a distinctly supporting role, and that it will be phased out as soon as it is no longer needed.	92	9
201407	1255	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Importantly, the set of principles is sufficiently flexible.	92	9
201407	1256	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	It allows us to learn and adjust along the way, and I think we should start with a 25 basis point spread between the IOER and overnight reverse repo rates.	92	9
201407	1257	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	If that is too much or too little to achieve monetary control, as we have been discussing quite a bit this morning, we can make adjustments.	92	9
201407	1258	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	And as we learn how our tools work in controlling the federal funds market, we can narrow the announced range for the federal funds rate.	92	9
201407	1259	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	I do want to emphasize something.	92	9
201407	1260	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	I was in support of a federal funds target range, a 25 basis point range in terms of our target.	92	9
201407	1261	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	That is basically just the reality, that in the current environment it is probably going to be very difficult to—or be impossible, maybe, to control the federal funds rate at a point target as we have done in the past.	92	9
201407	1262	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	I don’t think it would be advisable to go to a 50 basis point range or looser view of what our target is.	92	9
201407	1263	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	I think there’s a governance issue here, too.	92	9
201407	1264	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	The FOMC is making a policy decision.	92	9
201407	1265	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	We want a federal funds rate or short-term market rates trading in a certain area, and we definitely want to have the tools that allow us to achieve that goal.	92	9
201407	1266	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Finally, question 4, the design of the reverse repo facility should, for the most part, allow it to supplement the IOER rate in achieving monetary control while having adequate safeguards to preserve financial stability.	92	9
201407	1267	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	And again, I think the 25 basis point spread is a good place to begin, because just the economics of it will limit the desired take-up.	92	9
201407	1268	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, some caps on take-up also seem appropriate.	92	9
201407	1269	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	I agree with the points that Governors Powell and Tarullo made in their memo.	92	9
201407	1270	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Like some others who have spoken already, I don’t actually see the need or see that much benefit from the surge caps or the dynamic caps.	92	9
201407	1271	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	I think the overall cap achieves that goal.	92	9
201407	1272	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	But I recognize that others do like the belt-and-suspenders approach that the Federal Reserve prefers, and having a combination of dynamic and static caps seems to be a reasonable compromise between the need for monetary control and clear communication on the one hand and concerns around market functioning and financial stability on the other.	92	9
201407	1273	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	In terms of aggregate limits, it was unclear to me whether $500 billion was the right number in the beginning.	92	9
201407	1274	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	I think we do need more staff analysis to quantify these tradeoffs.	92	9
201407	1275	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	But it’s really going to be the real-world experience, I think, that is going to help us understand that.	92	9
201407	1276	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	And given the concerns about the potential size of the facility, again expressed by Governors Tarullo and Powell, it may make sense to start with somewhat lower caps than the $500 billion, that bind only occasionally.	92	9
201407	1277	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	We can revisit these decisions later.	92	9
201407	1278	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	That said, I don’t think it would be wise to lower the caps too far or to jettison the overnight reverse repo entirely, since that could materially interfere with control of the federal funds rate.	92	9
201407	1279	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, I want to talk just very briefly, but I think this is an important issue.	92	9
201407	1280	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	There are a number of commentators out there actively saying that the Federal Reserve cannot control interest rates with the $4½ trillion balance sheet.	92	9
201407	1281	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	This is not just a theoretical exercise.	92	9
201407	1282	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	This is a view that is expressed regularly out there, that we don’t have the ability to do that.	92	9
201407	1283	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	We can say we do, but I think an important part of this normalization statement is not only to state that we know how to do it, but to demonstrate how we are going to do it in a way that works from day one.	92	9
201407	1284	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	I think that is actually very important for confidence in the Federal Reserve, it’s very important for our credibility, but it is also very important for our ability to conduct monetary policy as appropriate for our monetary policy objectives.	92	9
201407	1285	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	So I think that the ON RRP provides a useful tool to not only assure ourselves that we actually have the tools to conduct monetary policy the way we need to, but also to assure the public that we have the tools.	92	9
201407	1286	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Again, I think it’s very important that as we go out the gate that we don’t stumble, because although you can easily sit here today and say, “Well, we can figure it out over the next couple of weeks,”	92	9
201407	1287	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	I do think that it would play to an already expressed view that the Federal Reserve doesn’t have the capability to control monetary policy.	92	9
201407	1288	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Regarding the idea of adding counterparty caps as well, I have to say that I already view this as a bit of a Rube Goldberg contraption, and with the dynamic caps, the static caps, all of the mathematics underneath that, I don’t think that we really need to be adding individual counterparty caps, or that maintaining the ones we have is necessary.	92	9
201407	1289	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	It likely would add to confusion and uncertainty.	92	9
201407	1290	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	And, again, it comes at some potential cost in terms of monetary control.	92	9
201407	1291	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	I think that the aggregate caps are all that we really need.	92	9
201407	1292	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	In terms of testing, I think that of course it is important that we thoughtfully and thoroughly test the caps that we plan to use in an appropriate time and in an appropriate way.	92	9
201407	1293	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	I agree with the comments that we don’t want to allow the testing to confuse or drive market participants to come to wrong conclusions.	92	9
201407	1294	2014-07-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	But, still, we do want to have a good understanding of how this will actually work.	92	9

201407	1308	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I think it was really quite productive, and I have benefited from that.	92	9
201407	1309	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I support a number of the features enumerated in the staff memos, and I disagree with some of the particulars.	92	9
201407	1310	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	For instance, I agree that using a range for the effective funds rate to communicate the stance of policy is the way policy should be conducted and communicated.	92	9
201407	1311	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I also agree that the primary tool for adjusting the funds rate should be changes in the IOER, at least until such a time that a smaller balance sheet allows us to return to a corridor system, and thus the targeted funds rate could be above IOER, which is something I have long advocated.	92	9
201407	1312	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I am less enthusiastic about a large role for the “on rip” or ON RRP or whatever—maybe it should be “ripoff,”	92	9
201407	1313	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I’m not exactly sure.	92	9
201407	1314	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	In any event, I would prefer not using it at all, if possible, and that there be no specific reference to it in the statement of principles.	92	9
201407	1315	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	We should simply refer to “other supplementary tools.”	92	9
201407	1316	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Many around this table have expressed reservations about this facility, and I share many of those concerns.	92	9
201407	1317	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Others believe that the facility could be useful if managed properly.	92	9
201407	1318	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I have doubts about managing it properly.	92	9
201407	1319	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I am greatly concerned about unintended consequences of such large interventions as anticipated.	92	9
201407	1320	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	However, if the facility is used, I’d prefer a much larger spread between the IOER and the ON RRP rates—say, 50 basis points—with a much lower overall limit and a cap of, say, $250 billion to $300 billion.	92	9
201407	1321	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Initially, I recommend we lift off without the use of the ON RRP facility.	92	9
201407	1322	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	We leave it where it is, go ahead and lift off.	92	9
201407	1323	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	This will allow us to test how effective the IOER is on its own at lifting rates.	92	9
201407	1324	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	If we’re unhappy with that outcome, then we could gradually increase the scale and operation of the ON RRP to begin closing the gap and narrowing the spread between the effective funds rate and IOER.	92	9
201407	1325	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	And it would be good if we could even shrink that spread gradually.	92	9
201407	1326	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	My own view is that I would be willing to tolerate more volatility and a bigger range for the funds rate than some around the table.	92	9
201407	1327	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	And I think we could do so and communicate it effectively if we are willing to, in fact, talk about that—that here is what we anticipate, here is the volatility that we anticipate.	92	9
201407	1328	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I think that would serve to mitigate claims that we can’t control rates.	92	9
201407	1329	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	But if we start off with a rather wider range, I think we can mitigate some of those communication concerns.	92	9
201407	1330	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	In any event, by only gradually introducing the facility over time, we also could learn a great deal about the sensitivity of the federal funds rate to the size and scale of the ON RRP program, and so forth.	92	9
201407	1331	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Further, as I said in my memo that I circulated before the meeting, I believe the overnight reverse repo market facility should be viewed as temporary and shelved when it is no longer needed.	92	9
201407	1332	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	The revised principles make this point very clearly, and I support that.	92	9
201407	1333	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	But I think it is easier said than done.	92	9
201407	1334	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	One of the things I worry about is that whatever particulars that we do have—for example, the spread, the cap, the size, the number of counterparties—will influence our ability to shelve the program.	92	9
201407	1335	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	That leads me to a preference to see us limit the counterparties rather than expand them, and make the caps smaller to keep the program of a small size, because as it expands and the counterparties grow, it will be harder and harder, I think, for us to convince ourselves to pull out of such a very large intervention and scale of operations.	92	9
201407	1336	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I think at the last meeting we talked a little bit about the possibility of limiting, for example, accessibility to government-only money market funds rather than all money market funds.	92	9
201407	1337	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	There may be dimensions like that which we should think about—limiting the number of counterparties.	92	9
201407	1338	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	At a minimum, I don’t think we should do anything about our counterparties today until we have more discussion about this.	92	9
201407	1339	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Regarding the dynamic caps, I don’t see a lot of reason for them.	92	9
201407	1340	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I’m not too concerned about the volatility on odd days, and I think we could over-engineer this process if we are not careful, again making it more difficult to shelve when the time comes.	92	9
201407	1341	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	The degree of interest rate control that was the primary concern in the memos was of the day-to-day variety and seeking to prevent volatility on certain days of the year, like quarter-end.	92	9
201407	1342	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	That kind of volatility has always existed in these markets.	92	9
201407	1343	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	It is not a new volatility, and I don’t see a particular concern for the conduct of monetary policy on those two or three days of the year.	92	9
201407	1344	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	In addition, we have so little knowledge of what it would take to keep the intraday effective funds rate trading within its target range, that I am reluctant, at least initially, to cede authority to the Chair to make intermeeting adjustments in the IOER or ON RRP rates, or caps.	92	9
201407	1345	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Altering the trading range of these rates could involve decisions reflecting a menu of choices, and I think that at least early on they should be made by the FOMC, if changes were deemed necessary.	92	9
201407	1346	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	And the question is partly, at what level do you begin to decide whether an intermeeting call is actually even necessary?	92	9
201407	1347	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Maybe we should just wait until the meeting.	92	9
201407	1348	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	But, again, if it’s deemed necessary for some reason.	92	9
201407	1349	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	As we learn more about how the federal funds rate reacts to changes in the IOER, I can see giving the Chair some authority on certain aspects of that, or perhaps the ON RRP rate, with limits during intermeeting periods, if we were more comfortable and we had learned more about how it was going to work.	92	9
201407	1350	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I have a few other concerns about the treatment of the balance sheet and the principles, as I alluded to earlier.	92	9
201407	1351	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	First, I believe that we should start shrinking the balance sheet sooner rather than later.	92	9
201407	1352	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Delay seems to accomplish very little in my mind, yet it will likely force us to raise rates higher and faster than we otherwise would choose to do under a smaller balance sheet.	92	9
201407	1353	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	At a minimum, I think we should remove the word “gradual” from the description of the path of the balance sheet, as we may find that constraining at some point.	92	9
201407	1354	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	The second part of that—in announcing we will not sell MBS, we prolong our credit allocation policy and favor housing credit at the expense of other sectors, as President Lacker’s comments so clearly enunciated.	92	9
201407	1355	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I would also add to that, though, that we also don’t know how the world is going to unfold.	92	9
201407	1356	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	We may find it appropriate and desirable to sell MBS at some point.	92	9
201407	1357	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I don’t think it is wise to make such blanket, unconditional statements about our future policies.	92	9
201407	1358	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	President Rosengren suggested that he didn’t like hardwired numbers in a set of principles.	92	9
201407	1359	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Well, zero is a hardwired number, and I’m pretty uncomfortable with that as a statement of principle.	92	9
201407	1360	2014-07-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Those are my remarks, Madam Chair.	92	9

201407	1365	2014-07-30	meeting	LOCKHART	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9

201407	1367	2014-07-30	meeting	LOCKHART	I’ve come to the view at this point in our deliberations on normalization that the wisest posture is to limit the role of the overnight reverse repo tool as much as possible.	92	9
201407	1368	2014-07-30	meeting	LOCKHART	That puts me in sympathy with the thrust of the broad concerns expressed by Governors Tarullo and Powell in their memo, President Plosser in his memo and his remarks, and the concern of President Kocherlakota in his memo.	92	9
201407	1369	2014-07-30	meeting	LOCKHART	Considering what I know now, I am comfortable with a limited and possibly transitional role for an overnight reverse repo facility, but I’m not comfortable with the prospect of a major, permanent, and institutionalized element of the short-term money markets and monetary control architecture.	92	9
201407	1370	2014-07-30	meeting	LOCKHART	To the extent that we’re firming up today, and in the near future, our thinking about the preferred approach, I favor a phased approach to implementation of an overnight reverse repo tool.	92	9
201407	1371	2014-07-30	meeting	LOCKHART	I prefer starting with an increase of the IOER rate and the federal funds rate range while holding the overnight reverse repo rate at or near current levels to see if IOER is strong enough to do the job.	92	9
201407	1372	2014-07-30	meeting	LOCKHART	I am not yet convinced that IOER will not work.	92	9
201407	1373	2014-07-30	meeting	LOCKHART	In reality, we won’t know for sure until we start to execute, and we’ll be learning by doing.	92	9
201407	1374	2014-07-30	meeting	LOCKHART	I acknowledge that the Committee’s credibility may be put in the balance by opting for measured escalation, but at this point, my sense is that a situation involving some trial and error can be managed.	92	9

201407	1391	2014-07-30	meeting	LOCKHART	That said, I have concerns about immediate implementation at liftoff, as I’ve already said, of a $500 billion facility priced at 25 basis points.	92	9

201407	1395	2014-07-30	meeting	LOCKHART	By initially holding the overnight reverse repo rate at its current level or close to that, we can see if the IOER increase alone has the hoped-for effect.	92	9
201407	1396	2014-07-30	meeting	LOCKHART	Apparently I have more confidence than others that IOER will work to raise the effective federal funds rate.	92	9
201407	1397	2014-07-30	meeting	LOCKHART	If IOER proves insufficient, the Committee or the Chair can walk the overnight reverse repo rate up based on assessment of timing requirements.	92	9
201407	1398	2014-07-30	meeting	LOCKHART	On the question of giving the Chair authority to make intermeeting period adjustments to IOER and overnight reverse repo rates as well as daily circuit breaker caps and an overall limit on take-up, I have no problem with tactical adjustments made at the discretion of the Chair to address intermittent, sporadic issues in the federal funds market.	92	9
201407	1399	2014-07-30	meeting	LOCKHART	If we experience persistent and material failures to maintain the funds rate within the target range, we would have deeper issues to address as a Committee, in my opinion.	92	9

201407	1402	2014-07-30	meeting	LOCKHART	But more generally my thinking is the Desk should design and come back to the Committee with tests in the spirit of moving the program to a point of operational readiness as a contingent tool.	92	9
201407	1403	2014-07-30	meeting	LOCKHART	This may fall short of the complete readiness and comprehensive communication to market participants the Desk feels is needed to protect against the perception of tentativeness that might undermine credibility.	92	9
201407	1404	2014-07-30	meeting	LOCKHART	Crafting guidance to the Desk and staff at this stage involves tradeoff judgments.	92	9
201407	1405	2014-07-30	meeting	LOCKHART	There is a tension between ensuring effectiveness of the tool and putting constraints on the program to balance off other concerns.	92	9
201407	1406	2014-07-30	meeting	LOCKHART	Boiled down, the effectiveness concern is the argument that if you take a tentative approach, it may not work.	92	9
201407	1407	2014-07-30	meeting	LOCKHART	I’m not convinced of that.	92	9
201407	1408	2014-07-30	meeting	LOCKHART	My starting point is the presumption that with effective communication that prepares markets for liftoff, followed by the decision to raise IOER and the federal funds rate range, the FOMC will get what it wants.	92	9

201407	1470	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	My comments are meant to be constructive within that context.	92	9
201407	1471	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	Let me address strategy and program design first, questions 1 and 4, and communications next, questions 2 and 3.	92	9
201407	1472	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	I broadly agree with the strategy outlined in the memo.	92	9
201407	1473	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	I favor using a target range for the funds rate as the primary means of setting and communicating the stance of policy and using the interest rate on excess reserves as the main tool for ensuring that the funds rate remains within the FOMC’s target range.	92	9
201407	1474	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	I think it’s going to be important in the initial stages of liftoff to show that we can raise the funds rate and hit our target range.	92	9
201407	1475	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	Otherwise we risk the credibility of that range and the creation of a lot of confusion about the path of monetary policy, both to be avoided.	92	9
201407	1476	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	It’s going to be important to communicate our tolerance for variation in the funds rate.	92	9
201407	1477	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	Whatever we come to agree about that tolerance, at this point we don’t know whether raising the IOER will be enough.	92	9
201407	1478	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	So I’m reluctant to take any of the other tools off the table, including term deposits, asset sales, and the overnight reverse repurchase facility.	92	9
201407	1479	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	That said, as I expressed at the last meeting, I do have concerns about the consequences of the ON RRPs for financial stability and market structure.	92	9
201407	1480	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	As I see it, the goal is to address those concerns by setting up the facility so that it can serve its purpose in providing backup support for the IOER, but in a way that appropriately limits the overall footprint of the program.	92	9
201407	1481	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	Now, I know we’re not expected to agree today on the numerical details, but I do want to say that I agree with the amendments to the staff proposal suggested by Governors Tarullo and Powell, and for similar reasons.	92	9
201407	1482	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	Lower caps that bind from time to time even when markets are not in distress will help to limit the program and overall reliance on it by market participants and serve to underscore that the facility is meant to play only a supporting and temporary role.	92	9
201407	1483	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	If it turns out we’re having difficulty keeping the funds rate above the lower edge of the target range, then we’re going to need to think about the tradeoffs between increased use of the reverse RPs, and a higher IOER rate, or using term deposits, which would mean higher payments to banks— and large banks at that, and foreign banks at that.	92	9
201407	1484	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	At that point, we’d also want to consider selling assets from our portfolio in a well-defined systematic path to lower the amount of excess reserves.	92	9
201407	1485	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	Given that the IOER rate and the ON RRP facility are going to be important aspects of normalization that the Committee as a whole will want to monitor, my preference would be, consistent with past practice, to ask that the Chair confer with the Committee, if feasible, before changes are made during an intermeeting period, especially an initial period in which we are all learning from experience.	92	9
201407	1486	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	Turning to communications, as I said at our last meeting, the communications surrounding the choices we make about normalization are going to be very important to how smoothly normalization will actually proceed.	92	9
201407	1487	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	I’m going to refrain from making detailed comments about the directive and the illustrative time-of-liftoff FOMC statement included in the memo.	92	9
201407	1488	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	More broadly, I support communicating policy in terms of the funds rate target and when a change is made, including language on the change and the related changes in the IOER and primary credit rates in the FOMC statement, and I prefer references to the ON RRPs to be in the directive to the Desk and not in the statement.	92	9
201407	1489	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	Because of the scrutiny the FOMC statement receives, major changes tend to be far and few between.	92	9
201407	1490	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	The beginning of normalization will require careful communication.	92	9
201407	1491	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	Accordingly, I see this as a rare opportunity to evaluate the current statement’s format and language, including the forward-guidance piece, and to consider improvements that will serve the Committee well as we navigate the turning tide in normalization.	92	9
201407	1492	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	Finally, regarding the draft normalization principles, I’m very supportive of providing a set of principles to the public in September.	92	9
201407	1493	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	I believe the revised principles circulated yesterday have captured many areas of agreement among participants and were responsive to many of the comments that I sent in on the earlier draft.	92	9
201407	1494	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	I think the challenge is to craft a statement of principles that appropriately balances generality and specificity to be a useful communications device.	92	9
201407	1495	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	I think the revisions moved us closer to that, and in hindsight, I guess I view the June 2011 exit-strategy principles as probably too tactical.	92	9
201407	1496	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	The separation of principles and tactics in the second version of the revision is probably beneficial, but if we go that route, then I think we should be more explicit in the final paragraph that principles are less likely to be revised than tactics.	92	9
201407	1497	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	I would support the white paper, which is mentioned in the memo, to explain the tools.	92	9
201407	1498	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	I would not be in favor of doing a consultation paper in advance.	92	9
201407	1499	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	I also want to note that in the revision in exhibit 5, there is now no mention of a target federal funds rate in the principles section.	92	9
201407	1500	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	That’s been moved to tactics.	92	9
201407	1501	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	I guess my understanding is that I thought we had agreed that we were going to have a target federal funds rate.	92	9
201407	1502	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	So if that’s a subtle decision that we’re not going to be targeting a funds rate, even as a range of a funds rate, I think that will be something we want to discuss more fully.	92	9
201407	1503	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	My understanding is that we had agreed, sort of in principle, to have a target, notwithstanding the difficulties of hitting the target.	92	9
201407	1504	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	One remaining issue is asset sales.	92	9
201407	1505	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	I think the revision does a better job of explaining our intention about asset sales.	92	9
201407	1506	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	My preference would be to leave ourselves a little more room to revise our sales strategy as we go forward.	92	9
201407	1507	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	We may decide that sales will be a useful tool in shrinking our balance sheet at a faster pace than currently anticipated.	92	9
201407	1508	2014-07-30	meeting	MESTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9

201407	1510	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	President Bullard.	92	9
201407	1511	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201407	1512	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	I have three main comments, which I’ll list here, and then I’ll provide some background on my comments.	92	9
201407	1513	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	First, I think the federal funds rate is overemphasized as the key policy rate in the approach to normalization outlined in the two staff memos for this meeting.	92	9
201407	1514	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	I will suggest that it may be prudent to de-emphasize references to the federal funds rate as the key policy rate during this period, and in this regard I share some of the views of President Rosengren.	92	9
201407	1515	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	This is just going to follow on some of the comments I made at the previous meeting.	92	9
201407	1516	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	Second, I would prefer to make some changes to the restated normalization principles to bring them closer to what the Committee agreed to in 2011.	92	9
201407	1517	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	I would prefer to say much less concerning the federal funds rate.	92	9
201407	1518	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	I think we should handle reinvestment as we did in 2011, and like President Mester, I think we should maintain more optionality for selling assets.	92	9
201407	1519	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	And third, in other areas, I’m broadly supportive of the approach to normalization and of the proposed design of the overnight reverse repurchase facility.	92	9
201407	1520	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	Let me now just walk through the questions that were asked in order.	92	9
201407	1521	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	On question 1— which concerns general support for the method of conducting monetary policy during normalization as described in the staff memos and also whether the Chair should have authority to change the IOER, the overnight reverse repurchase rate, or the caps on an intermeeting basis in order to keep the effective federal funds rate within the target range—in broad terms I’m supportive of using IOER and the proposed overnight RRP facility to normalize interest rates.	92	9
201407	1522	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	My main objection is that I do not think we can afford to emphasize the federal funds rate as much as it is emphasized in these memos as the primary tool of monetary policy.	92	9
201407	1523	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	The federal funds market is not, at the present time, a sufficiently robust market on which to base United States monetary policy.	92	9
201407	1524	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	What we are proposing is the federal funds rate on crutches.	92	9
201407	1525	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	The federal funds rate today is determined by a small number of idiosyncratic players, and movements in the effective rate can be idiosyncratic.	92	9
201407	1526	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	There is also some small chance that the market would cease to exist altogether during the period of normalization.	92	9
201407	1527	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	By contrast, the IOER applies to reserve holdings in the banking system and the overnight RRP facility touches on a broad range of institutions.	92	9
201407	1528	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	In short, the federal funds rate is a rate that does not matter in a macroeconomic sense.	92	9
201407	1529	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	It is the IOER and the ON RRP rates that matter, macroeconomically speaking.	92	9
201407	1530	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	Of these two, the overnight reverse repurchase rate is probably the more important.	92	9
201407	1531	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	Let’s think about the federal funds rate as dominated by noise trading.	92	9
201407	1532	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	The staff analysis suggests that, should the federal funds rate trade outside of the range assigned by the FOMC, the reaction may be to change the IOER rate, the overnight RRP rate, or both, to encourage  federal funds trading within the target range.	92	9
201407	1533	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	I find this suggestion especially worrisome.	92	9
201407	1534	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	It would mean that noise trading in the federal funds market would be a driver of US monetary policy because idiosyncratic trades occurring there would induce changes in policy rates of far more import, namely the IOER and the overnight RRP rates.	92	9
201407	1535	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	That could have important macroeconomic effects, but in response to noise trades.	92	9
201407	1536	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	What can be done about this?	92	9
201407	1537	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	I suggest that we do not put heavy emphasis on the federal funds rate as the key policy rate.	92	9
201407	1538	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	Instead, we should say that all three rates are important and that we expect the federal funds rate to trade between the IOER and the overnight RRP rates.	92	9
201407	1539	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	We should then say that if the federal funds rate does not trade between the two rates because of idiosyncratic factors in that market, we may base policy solely on the IOER rate and the overnight RRP rate in the future.	92	9
201407	1540	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	This modified approach might keep us from changing rates of consequence in response to vagaries in the federal funds market.	92	9
201407	1541	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	It follows from these comments that I do not support giving the Chair authority to change the IOER rate, the overnight RRP rate, or caps in order to keep the federal funds rate in a specified trading range.	92	9
201407	1542	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	Instead, should the federal funds rate consistently trade outside the Committee’s specified range, the Committee should convene and consider putting out a statement that the key policy rates are the IOER and the overnight RRP rates.	92	9
201407	1543	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	I would keep the overnight RRP rate in this situation, as I feel it intersects with a broader set of counterparties than reliance on IOER alone.	92	9
201407	1544	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	The US banking system is only 20 percent of US financial intermediation, and in the future we’re probably going to have to do better than that in order to influence short-term interest rates.	92	9
201407	1545	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	In short, if the proposed system does not work as intended, I think we will have little choice but to de-emphasize the federal funds rate as the key policy rate.	92	9
201407	1546	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	Let me now turn briefly to financial-stability issues.	92	9
201407	1547	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	I have some sympathy with President Kocherlakota’s call for a fuller discussion with the private sector concerning the possible implications of the overnight RRP facility for financial stability.	92	9
201407	1548	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	It is certainly a fair comment that we do not, at present, have a good handle on the possible financial-stability effects of the overnight RRP facility.	92	9
201407	1549	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	Still, my bottom line on this issue is that in a true financial crisis, the Committee will have to make decisions about appropriate actions to take, and that it would be difficult to script those actions sitting here today.	92	9
201407	1550	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	Since this is the case, I prefer to lean against allowing financial-stability concerns to get in the way of implementing monetary policy during the period of policy normalization.	92	9
201407	1551	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	On question 2, which concerns proposed communications, I’m broadly supportive of the proposal as in the staff’s suggestion.	92	9
201407	1552	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	On question 3, which concerns newly proposed normalization principles, I have the following comments.	92	9
201407	1553	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	Bullet 2 of the proposed principles, along with the sub-bullets, mentions the federal funds rate five times.	92	9
201407	1554	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	Today’s updated versions are not that much different.	92	9
201407	1555	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	In my view, this is way overdone.	92	9
201407	1556	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	I propose simply eliminating the three sub-bullets of bullet 2 in exhibit 4.	92	9
201407	1557	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	The federal funds rate would then just be mentioned once in conjunction with other short-term interest rates.	92	9
201407	1558	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	I think this would more correctly characterize the state of affairs, which I see as moving the three interest rates in tandem if everything goes according to plan, and I think it would better reflect that reality.	92	9
201407	1559	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	As written, the bullets convey far too much technical detail, really tactics and not principles.	92	9
201407	1560	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	If we do go to exhibit 5 instead, I would eliminate the tactics section altogether.	92	9
201407	1561	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	On reinvestment, I suggest simply keeping bullet 2 from the 2011 exit principles.	92	9
201407	1562	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	One issue with these principles is how useful and credible they are if the Committee is willing to shift to a new set of principles as the time for implementation draws near.	92	9
201407	1563	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	Bullet 2 from 2011 would restate that the Committee “will likely first cease reinvesting some or all payments of principal on the securities holdings in the SOMA.”	92	9
201407	1564	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	As I argued last time, I think it would be useful for the Committee to be able to cease reinvestment as an intermediate step between the ending of the QE program and the date of first liftoff in the policy rate.	92	9
201407	1565	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	Also, this could be done in a more managed way by partially ceasing reinvestment or by reinvesting in shorter-term Treasury securities and partially undoing our twist operation that we did earlier in the period of unconventional monetary policy.	92	9
201407	1566	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	I do not think that the macroeconomic impact would be large, but I do think it would help the credibility of the Committee by beginning to shrink the balance sheet, even if it were in a passive way.	92	9
201407	1567	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	I think it would also signal that the Committee felt comfortable enough with the state of the economy that the time of policy rate liftoff was drawing near.	92	9
201407	1568	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	I would also remove the second sub-bullet in the proposed normalization principles concerning the sales of MBS.	92	9
201407	1569	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	In this area, I agree with some of the comments of President Lockhart.	92	9
201407	1570	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	I see no reason to commit to this in these principles.	92	9
201407	1571	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	I prefer to keep options on the table.	92	9
201407	1572	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	The situation might change as we go down the road and we decide what we want to do.	92	9
201407	1573	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	I also agreed with President Fisher’s suggestion that we could add a clause, at a minimum, to the MBS feature in this statement.	92	9
201407	1574	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	The clause was, as I recall it, to say that if the housing market was quite robust, then possibly we would consider selling MBS.	92	9
201407	1575	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	I think we could have something like that included.	92	9
201407	1576	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	In general, in very broad terms I would actually prefer to keep the 2011 exit principles as opposed to moving to the 2014 set of principles.	92	9
201407	1577	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	It seems to me that we will be gaining very little while possibly sowing considerable confusion with the new set of exit principles.	92	9
201407	1578	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	Question 4 concerns the broad design of the overnight reverse repurchase facility.	92	9
201407	1579	2014-07-30	meeting	BULLARD	I’m okay on most of these dimensions.	92	9

201407	1601	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	President Kocherlakota.	92	9
201407	1602	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201407	1603	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	And like others, I’d like to thank the staff for their ongoing excellent work on a very challenging area of inquiry.	92	9
201407	1604	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As you suggested, Madam Chair, I think the most important issue facing the Committee right now is whether or not to commit to the use of the facility—as we call it, somewhat ominously, in Minnesota—in September.	92	9
201407	1605	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The memo I sent to the Committee on Saturday provides my view on that issue, so I’m going to elaborate on the key point that I made.	92	9
201407	1606	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	And when I talk about committing to the use of the facility, what I am referring to is specific mention of it in the normalization principles that we would be releasing in September, and I do support the idea of releasing normalization principles at that time.	92	9
201407	1607	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	To go back to the memo that we circulated on Saturday, we have heard from both staff and FOMC participants that the facility could have adverse effects on the industrial structure of short-term funding markets and on financial stability.	92	9
201407	1608	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Unfortunately, we have relatively little information with which to judge the magnitude of these downside risks and the effectiveness of possible mitigants of, for example, the kind that Governors Powell and Tarullo suggested.	92	9
201407	1609	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We do have data from tests of the facility.	92	9
201407	1610	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	These tests are necessarily incomplete.	92	9
201407	1611	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	They cannot tell us the consequences of a larger or more permanent facility, nor how the facility would affect the economy in the event of a financial crisis—that’s what I have in my notes here, but actually, the testing period has been a time of very low volatility overall in financial markets, so we actually don’t even have a good test of how it would fare in what I would call a more normal period of volatility.	92	9
201407	1612	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think we have received outstanding support, analysis, and advice from the Federal Reserve System staff.	92	9
201407	1613	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Nonetheless, I think we could benefit from receiving input from experts outside our own organization.	92	9
201407	1614	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As I indicated in the memo on Saturday, I think it would be useful for the FOMC to gather more information about the facility before committing to its use.	92	9
201407	1615	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In the memo, I recommended the Committee collect this information by issuing a public consultation paper, seeking public comment on that paper, and convening a conference of outside experts on financial stability and short-term funding markets to discuss it.	92	9
201407	1616	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think we do a lot of this information-gathering in a very informal way.	92	9
201407	1617	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think the Desk in New York does a great job with their contacts.	92	9
201407	1618	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	All of us, I presume, are reaching out to our contacts, some with small banks, some with large banks, and with other financial market participants.	92	9
201407	1619	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	This is just a systematizing of that process and opening it up to the public for this particular facility.	92	9
201407	1620	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	This is not a discussion of the stance of monetary policy.	92	9
201407	1621	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The independence of this organization does require the kind of isolation that we impose on that process.	92	9
201407	1622	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It is, rather, a discussion of a particular tool, a particular enhancement of the tools that we have available to us.	92	9
201407	1623	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	And as I say, I think it is merely making transparent and systematizing a process that we are already undergoing.	92	9
201407	1624	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I indicated in the memo that I think there is a time frame in which all three of these steps could be accomplished by the end of October, in time for a decision at our December meeting.	92	9
201407	1625	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	If you wanted to drop one of the three steps, I think convening a conference is not an essential feature here.	92	9
201407	1626	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think the public consultation paper and the commentary on that one is the best.	92	9
201407	1627	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, these three steps would give us more assurance that whatever choice we make is based on the best information and analysis available in the time that we need to make a decision.	92	9
201407	1628	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think engaging the public in this way would enhance our reputation for transparency and would help us learn about the likely responses to our potential use of this tool.	92	9
201407	1629	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Some of them would be political, but some of them, just from market participants, about who is going to be hurt and who is going to benefit—I think we should have information about that before making judgments.	92	9
201407	1630	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, I have been emphasizing our need to learn about the possible downside risks of the facility.	92	9
201407	1631	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The reason I have been doing that emphasis is because coming into this meeting, I saw the main decision before us right now as being whether to commit to the use of this tool in September.	92	9
201407	1632	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	When you are making a commitment, the downside risks are the more relevant factor than the upside risks.	92	9
201407	1633	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But the information-gathering that I propose in my memo would have broader uses.	92	9
201407	1634	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	And this gets to a point that I think President Lockhart was alluding to in his remarks.	92	9

201407	1636	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I don’t feel I know enough to make that judgment either.	92	9
201407	1637	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	One of the ways in which my staff helped me prepare for this meeting is by actually having a debate about whether or not we should have the overnight reverse repo facility.	92	9
201407	1638	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	One of my staff was able to fulfill a lifelong dream and play Bill Dudley in real life.	92	9
201407	1639	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	[Laughter]	92	9

201407	1642	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Even if we decide to use the facility as we go through liftoff, we are going to face some key choices about how to use it.	92	9
201407	1643	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Right now, we are very nervous and scared because we don’t have enough information, and so we are trying to scale back and commit ourselves to scaling it back.	92	9
201407	1644	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So we are going to commit to use it and commit not to use very much of it.	92	9
201407	1645	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think if we go through the information-gathering steps, we might well learn information that would help us become more confident with using the facility, as well as information that might help us learn about mitigation of downside risks.	92	9
201407	1646	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So my suggested approach, I think, leads to fairly short answers to the questions posed to us by staff.	92	9
201407	1647	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I am not supportive of the draft normalization principles as written, because I believe it is premature to be mentioning the overnight facility at this time.	92	9

201407	1658	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Let me make three quick comments here.	92	9

201407	1666	2014-07-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	And President Rosengren’s little experiment of raising the IOER in a technical way— of course, that’s the whole art—how do you tell people it’s technical?	92	9
