201407	1673	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	Vice Chairman.	92	9
201407	1674	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	Thank you.	92	9
201407	1675	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I am generally comfortable with the approach outlined in the staff memos.	92	9
201407	1676	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I do want to compliment the staff on the quality of the work.	92	9
201407	1677	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	It is no easy task to take the musings of 17 different FOMC participants, try to boil that down to a coherent proposal that we could all agree to.	92	9
201407	1678	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I’m going to try to address the major substantive issues, so where I’m silent you can assume that I am in agreement with the staff proposal.	92	9
201407	1679	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	The first major point concerns the use of the overnight RRP facility.	92	9
201407	1680	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	As I see it, the point of the facility is to help ensure that we have adequate monetary policy control.	92	9
201407	1681	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	That is, we are able to control the constellation of money market rates sufficiently well so that we can affect financial conditions in a way consistent with the Committee’s dual mandate goals.	92	9
201407	1682	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I agree with others that we should rely on the overnight RRP facility only as much as needed to ensure adequate monetary policy control.	92	9
201407	1683	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	If we could have sufficient control with the overnight RRP, with a relatively wide spread and small take-up, that would be a good outcome.	92	9
201407	1684	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	And if we could ultimately move to just having the IOER do all the lifting, that would probably be even a better outcome.	92	9
201407	1685	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	My own view is that the staff proposal, starting with 25 basis point spread, is a reasonable starting point.	92	9
201407	1686	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	It seems likely to generate sufficient monetary policy control while keeping the footprint of the overnight RRP facility quite small.	92	9
201407	1687	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	But I think we have to view this as just a starting point, because we are making a guess about what the optimal tradeoff is between monetary control and the size and footprint of the facility.	92	9
201407	1688	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I could imagine we could find that we have excellent control at a 25 basis point spread, and if we did that, we might consider widening the spread to further reduce the size of the footprint of the facility.	92	9
201407	1689	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	Conversely, if we find that our monetary control is less than anticipated and the take-up of the facility isn’t very large, you might consider that narrowing the spread and accepting a somewhat larger take-up through the overnight RRP facility is appropriate.	92	9
201407	1690	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, there is a legitimate question of how to arrive at this optimal tradeoff between control and footprint.	92	9
201407	1691	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	And around the table people have said, “Well, we could conceivably start by just raising the IOER and leaving the overnight RRP rate unchanged at 5 basis points, and see if that was sufficient for monetary policy control.”	92	9
201407	1692	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	But to me, I think that raises the risk of a messy liftoff.	92	9
201407	1693	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	It seems to me it would be better to start with something like the staff proposal, the 25 basis point spread, and then evaluate whether the spread could be widened, and sufficient monetary policy control achieved, by leaning more heavily on the IOER.	92	9
201407	1694	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	Initially, I have two goals—minimize the risk on liftoff with respect to monetary policy control, and have the opportunity to gain more information about the tradeoff between spread size and monetary policy control.	92	9
201407	1695	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	And then we use that to decide our subsequent adjustments.	92	9
201407	1696	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	With respect to the long-term use of the overnight RRP facility, I very much see this as a supplemental and temporary tool of monetary policy.	92	9
201407	1697	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	And to ensure it stays that way, I think we have to be explicit about that in our principles.	92	9
201407	1698	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	So I am very happy with the revised principles.	92	9
201407	1699	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I also think it is important to recognize that it is highly likely that the need for an overnight RRP facility should lessen as the balance sheet starts to normalize because reserves will become scarcer and arbitrage should work better when that occurs.	92	9
201407	1700	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I think we should understand that the overnight RRP facility is really most important when the balance sheet is at its biggest point, where we are today.	92	9
201407	1701	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	With respect to the caps, I thought that the staff made a very compelling case for both an aggregate cap and a circuit breaker limit on daily movement and activity.	92	9
201407	1702	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	But if we really are going to set the facility so the aggregate use isn’t that large, I think the incremental benefit of having a circuit breaker is pretty small.	92	9
201407	1703	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	If we end up with a facility that has a cap of $300 billion or $400 billion and usage of $150 billion to $200 billion, that $150 billion of headroom—you just don’t gain that much by having that circuit breaker cap if you only have $150 billion of headroom to play with.	92	9
201407	1704	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	So I don’t think that incremental benefit is very large.	92	9
201407	1705	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, with respect to the issue of the size of the facility, I think it is really too soon to be clear about what that aggregate cap should be.	92	9
201407	1706	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	When we introduce this, we really want to make sure that we have sufficient headroom so that when the facility is introduced you are not running into the cap frequently.	92	9
201407	1707	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	If you are running into the cap frequently, then you are actually going to lose monetary policy control.	92	9
201407	1708	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	So to go back to the Powell-Tarullo memo, if we had a $300 billion cap and the take-up of the facility was $150 billion, I think that would work very well, because you would have $150 billion of headroom.	92	9
201407	1709	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	But if you were in the less fortunate circumstance of April, or maybe the take-up of the facility was $250 billion and the cap was $300 billion, that is not a lot of headroom.	92	9
201407	1710	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	You’d be sacrificing a lot of potential monetary policy control.	92	9
201407	1711	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I think that we should continue to run the experiment over the next six to nine months, and we will learn a lot more about what the expected size of the facility is likely to be.	92	9
201407	1712	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	We should try to do that in a form that is closest to how we think the facility will actually work when it is implemented, not in a testing phase but in the liftoff phase.	92	9
201407	1713	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	And I think as we do that, then we can sort of decide what is an appropriate cap at the time of liftoff to make sure that there is sufficient headroom so you don’t hit the cap a lot inadvertently and undermine monetary policy control, but not have a cap that is so high, way higher than necessary, that then would send the wrong message to market participants about how important this facility is supposed to be over the longer term.	92	9
201407	1714	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	The third point I would make with respect to the revised exit principles is that I think we should be explicit that we do plan to let the balance sheet normalize primarily by securities maturing and running off.	92	9
201407	1715	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I’m happy to entertain language that gives us a little bit more flexibility than what we have right now, but I think that if we really think that the balance sheet is going to be set mostly on autopilot, if we really think that’s the most likely scenario, then I think we should be clear to people that that’s how we are going to behave.	92	9
201407	1716	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I completely agree that the world can change and we could decide that we want to use the balance sheet in a more active way.	92	9
201407	1717	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	But if most of us really think that it’s going to be on autopilot, I think it is better to communicate that as an expectation to markets, because otherwise it is just going to be an open issue and people are going to be musing about it and asking questions of the Chair at every press conference.	92	9
201407	1718	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I think it would better to tamp that down a bit.	92	9
201407	1719	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	The fourth point I’d make is about making the federal funds rate more robust.	92	9
201407	1720	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	We have essentially deferred the discussion about what to do with the federal funds rate to a future meeting, but it’s pretty important.	92	9
201407	1721	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I mean, if the overnight RRP counterparty list ultimately is going to expand further, the arbitrage from the GSEs to the banks, particularly foreign banking organizations, could lessen further, diminishing the volume of the federal funds rate transactions and making the federal funds rate even more idiosyncratic.	92	9
201407	1722	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, to me, the way out of this dilemma is not to move away from the federal funds rate as a target but to change the concept of what we target to an overnight borrowing rate that includes Eurodollar borrowings undertaken by US banks and foreign banks operating in the United States.	92	9
201407	1723	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I don’t think that is very controversial, if we were to move to that.	92	9
201407	1724	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I think it would make a much more robust instrument in terms of what we’re targeting.	92	9
201407	1725	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	The trickier issue is if we do move to this new borrowing rate, what do we call it?	92	9
201407	1726	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	Do we have the old effective funds rate and the old definition?	92	9
201407	1727	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	Do we also then have this new rate, or do we just move to a new definition of the federal funds rate?	92	9
201407	1728	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	So that’s something I think we really do need to talk about at a future meeting.	92	9
201407	1729	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	This is also very relevant in terms of all of the discussion of reference rates and all of the trillions of dollars of derivatives contracts that reference the federal funds rate.	92	9
201407	1730	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	It is not just a monetary policy issue; it is also an important issue with respect to reference rates.	92	9
201407	1731	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	Finally, on the issue of the timing of redemptions, I’d just reiterate what I said at the June meeting.	92	9
201407	1732	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I think ending reinvestments before raising short-term rates could conceivably delay liftoff in certain states of the world.	92	9
201407	1733	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	And I think that would be unfortunate, because it seems to me that getting off the zero lower bound is completely possible, consistent with our dual mandate objectives, and is important in order to regain monetary policy flexibility.	92	9
201407	1734	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I also think that if we delay ending reinvestment until after liftoff, it will simplify our communications.	92	9
201407	1735	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	There will be only one moving part, short-term interest rates, rather than two.	92	9
201407	1736	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	So I very much favor ending the reinvestment after liftoff rather than before.	92	9
201407	1737	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I think Richard Fisher has suggested “shortly after.”	92	9
201407	1738	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I think that is a little too prescriptive.	92	9
201407	1739	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I can imagine a situation where we lift off, the market reacts violently, we have a repeat of the taper tantrum, and then we have redemptions ending automatically shortly thereafter.	92	9
201407	1740	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	That would be, I think, not such a pleasant place to be.	92	9
201407	1741	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, as far as this issue of giving discretion to the Chair, I think it is completely reasonable to give discretion to the Chair about the tactics needed to keep the federal funds rate target in its range.	92	9
201407	1742	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I think it is completely unreasonable to delegate to the Chair changes in the federal funds rate target rate.	92	9
201407	1743	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	So I would discriminate between giving discretion to the Chair to move the target range around from making tactical choices in terms of IOER or the spread between overnight RRP and IOER to keep the funds rate in its range.	92	9
201407	1744	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	It seems to me like that does not require a videoconference for that sort of tactical change.	92	9
201407	1745	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	The Desk periodically makes decisions.	92	9
201407	1746	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I mean, back when we were running a corridor system, we had to make decisions every day about what intervention was appropriate to keep the federal funds rate at its target.	92	9
201407	1747	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	And we did not have a videoconference every day to address, “Should we do a system of overnight RRP?	92	9
201407	1748	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	Should we do customer RP?”	92	9
201407	1749	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I think the kind of things that we are talking about delegating to the Chair are the things of that nature—how we used to run a corridor system.	92	9
201407	1750	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	So I think delegating to the Chair the tactics of how you keep the federal funds rate in its range is completely reasonable, in my opinion.	92	9

201407	1778	2014-07-30	meeting	FISCHER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201407	1779	2014-07-30	meeting	FISCHER	There have been two tensions driving this discussion.	92	9
201407	1780	2014-07-30	meeting	FISCHER	One is the need to demonstrate or to have the ability to run monetary policy, by which I mean being able to hit our interest rate, and I’ll explain why I think that matters in a moment, versus concerns about are we inventing a Frankenstein monster called ON RRP, or whatever set of initials we want to use for this thing.	92	9
201407	1781	2014-07-30	meeting	FISCHER	That’s one of the tensions.	92	9
201407	1782	2014-07-30	meeting	FISCHER	The other is a tension over how much to try to predetermine future choices.	92	9
201407	1783	2014-07-30	meeting	FISCHER	Let me start with the need to demonstrate the ability to run monetary policy.	92	9
201407	1784	2014-07-30	meeting	FISCHER	This institution could have been, if it had not handled this crisis well—and I mean the crisis after September 2008—in very bad shape today and thought of as incompetent.	92	9
201407	1785	2014-07-30	meeting	FISCHER	It wasn’t incompetent.	92	9

201407	1798	2014-07-30	meeting	FISCHER	And I think we just need to assure ourselves that we can do it.	92	9
201407	1799	2014-07-30	meeting	FISCHER	So when it comes down to the choice between using the overnight reverse repo facility and having more certainty about our capacity to effect the target which we have chosen to continue to use, despite some concerns that were expressed—I think validly—around this table about whether this market will survive, I think we have to come down on the side of going with the overnight reverse repo facility and the 25 basis point range that has been suggested.	92	9
201407	1800	2014-07-30	meeting	FISCHER	If we were a private group working something out, there could be attractions in the “let’s try this and let’s go ahead and gradually improve it” approach.	92	9

201407	1874	2014-07-30	meeting	TARULLO	And that consistency sort of fell under the theme of what I would term the “bias of first impressions.”	92	9
201407	1875	2014-07-30	meeting	TARULLO	And it kind of captures the tension, I think, that Governor Fischer was talking about a moment ago.	92	9
201407	1876	2014-07-30	meeting	TARULLO	I think, as you all know from my June remarks and from the memo that Jay and I sent around, I have been very concerned with the financial stability, financial structure implications of the ON RRP facility.	92	9
201407	1877	2014-07-30	meeting	TARULLO	And many of the suggestions which we made in that memo—some of which might well be, as a technical matter, redundant—were designed to fashion the first impression that people have of the facility, and that is to say, a facility which was bound by a number of constraints and so was highly unlikely to develop into a key ongoing part of financial markets and was highly unlikely to serve as the basis for a business model of a particular kind of money market fund.	92	9
201407	1878	2014-07-30	meeting	TARULLO	But alongside that first impression is the first impression of our liftoff decision.	92	9
201407	1879	2014-07-30	meeting	TARULLO	And as President Williams and Governor Fischer have, I think, very convincingly argued, there is going to be enormous attention and focus on that first move, whether we like it or not.	92	9
201407	1880	2014-07-30	meeting	TARULLO	And we can sit here and say, “Ah, you know, we can adjust later, we don’t need to quite get there right away, we know there will be some movement in rates up and down the yield curve.”	92	9

201407	1919	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	Let me start with aggregate caps, and I commit that I will come in under a 500-word cap, given how late we are in the process.	92	9
201407	1920	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	Generally speaking, I support finalizing a plan to be announced in September that addresses the key elements of a monetary policy normalization framework.	92	9
201407	1921	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	I think it’s really important to send a signal that careful preparations are underway for the normalization of the stance and conduct of monetary policy once the data warrant it.	92	9
201407	1922	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	I put a very high premium on establishing, at the outset, the credibility of our ability to execute that plan, and everything follows from that.	92	9
201407	1923	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	Due to the unprecedented size of reserves in the system, I think it is critically important to demonstrate at the very outset that we can exert effective monetary control as we come off the zero lower bound.	92	9
201407	1924	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	I have to say, I didn’t actually understand the line of reasoning being pursued earlier that it might not matter if we fail to hit the target range for the federal funds rate, and that we could simply keep trying until we did.	92	9
201407	1925	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	Given that we are in completely uncharted territory, and there is substantial concern and commentary in the markets, and, more broadly, that we won’t be able to achieve our stated goals, it seems to me to be of utmost importance that market participants have full confidence at the outset that we can effectively influence the path of short-term rates.	92	9
201407	1926	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	I think we only have to look around the world at recent episodes in which central banks have failed to do that to see how very costly it is to regain credibility after a misstep.	92	9
201407	1927	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	So I would prefer to start more cautiously and widen over time, rather than the reverse, which some have suggested, of starting a little looser, experimenting, and then thinking we can get tighter.	92	9
201407	1928	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	The critical importance of credible execution leads me to strongly support continuing with a range as opposed to a point target for the federal funds rate.	92	9
201407	1929	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	In addition, I would support maintaining the federal funds rate as the focus, recognizing that this market is fairly unusual and thinly traded at the moment.	92	9
201407	1930	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	Nonetheless, there are substantial benefits, I think, in maintaining a policy framework that is familiar under circumstances that are, in all other respects, not at all familiar.	92	9
201407	1931	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	Second, the critical importance of establishing credibility argues strongly for employing the overnight reverse repo facility as a floor during the launch and initial stages, while making clear this is a subsidiary tool to the IOER.	92	9
201407	1932	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	The concerns that have been stated here, I think, are very real—concerns about ensuring that this instrument is designed in a way that its presence doesn’t alter the market structure, and it doesn’t amplify run risk.	92	9
201407	1933	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	It strikes me that the proposal on the table does the appropriate balancing between the need for effective monetary control and avoiding those two very important risks.	92	9
201407	1934	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	In particular, I think the language that has been artfully crafted to establish clearly at the outset that the overnight reverse repo facility will be used only to the extent and for the duration necessary to exercise effective monetary policy control is very important.	92	9
201407	1935	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	The proposal for an aggregate cap, together with the ability to widen the spread, and then the language that I just referenced, adequately addresses the financial-stability and market structure risks.	92	9
201407	1936	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	I agree with the Chair’s suggestion to defer questions on the size of the cap, pending further analysis once the decision here is clear.	92	9
201407	1937	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	With regard to the spread, I think the proposed initial one-for-one correspondence between the target range for the federal funds rate and the spread between the IOER and the overnight reverse repo rates has a certain appealing elegance.	92	9
201407	1938	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	Nonetheless, I would at least presume that we have in mind that over time, as reserve balances diminish, that increasingly the federal funds rate is going to trade closer to the top of that range, increasingly anchored by the IOER, and that we will progressively widen the spread between IOER and the overnight reverse repo rates in order to further downplay the role of the latter rate, even as we might over time be tightening the range for the federal funds rate, so as to gradually phase out this facility altogether.	92	9
201407	1939	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	With regard to intermeeting adjustments, the proposal to delegate authority to the Chair seems to me eminently practical.	92	9
201407	1940	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	The one thing that I would suggest, having listened to the intensity of this engagement for two meetings now, and to the very good questions that are being raised, is that I think it might be valuable to provide the participants, the Committee members, an opportunity to get on the phone or a videoconference to consult in advance, not for decisionmaking purposes, but so as to give members of this Committee more of a real-time sense of how the markets are adjusting to the monetary policy framework at moments when it isn’t actually performing as was anticipated or projected.	92	9
201407	1941	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	Finally, on the reinvestment, I think the language gets it just about right.	92	9
201407	1942	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	I read it as preserving constructive ambiguity to have the debate about sales versus runoff at a later date.	92	9
201407	1943	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	I think the real news here is to clarify that liftoff will take place before reinvestment ceases.	92	9
201407	1944	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	And that too, I think, follows very straightforwardly and compellingly from the critical importance of reestablishing effective monetary control.	92	9
201407	1945	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	I think that sequence is just a logical follow-on from the primacy that we are placing on monetary control.	92	9
201407	1946	2014-07-30	meeting	BRAINARD	That’s it.	92	9
201407	1947	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	Well, thank you, everybody.	92	9
201407	1948	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	I really appreciate your comments.	92	9
201407	1949	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	I think we have had another productive discussion, and obviously a wide range of views have been expressed.	92	9
201407	1950	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	To wrap up, I thought I might try to summarize where I think we stand.	92	9
201407	1951	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	On the approach to normalization, I heard widespread support for the overall approach that staff have proposed.	92	9
201407	1952	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	That includes retaining the federal funds rate as our key policy rate and continuing to target a 25 basis point range for this rate during the process of normalization.	92	9
201407	1953	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	I also heard considerable support for using IOER as our main tool to raise and control rates.	92	9
201407	1954	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	Initially, we would set this rate at the top of our target range for the federal funds rate, but we certainly could make adjustments over time, if necessary, to help keep the federal funds rate within the target range.	92	9
201407	1955	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	On redemptions, I think the majority seems comfortable ceasing reinvestment after liftoff rather than before, but I certainly heard a few of you who think the opposite:  Ceasing reinvestment first is the better approach.	92	9
201407	1956	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	Views on the use of the overnight RRP facility were passionate and mixed, but I think there is broad support for the notion that the facility should play some role—although a carefully calibrated one—in the normalization process in order to improve our control over the funds rate.	92	9
201407	1957	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	I think many of you agree, and I would concur, that the presumption should be that the overnight RRP facility will not be permanent, and that our communications need to reflect that, as in the revised normalization principles document that staff circulated.	92	9
201407	1958	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	I think your concerns about the facility incline most of you to keep the overall size of the facility on the smaller end of the spectrum, but the size should be sufficient to afford some control over rates.	92	9
201407	1959	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	I think where we have come out is that we have agreed that we have a bit of time before we need to set numerical parameters, and that we can benefit from further analysis and testing and come back to this, and also perhaps reconsider, especially if we end up with a somewhat lower cap, whether we actually need two caps, both an overall cap and also a dynamic cap.	92	9
201407	1960	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	With respect to the spread between IOER and the overnight RRP rates, I heard support for a relatively wide spread, as proposed by the staff, and it is something that will also serve to limit the size of the facility.	92	9
201407	1961	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	Now, conceivably, as many of you pointed out, the spread can be wider, it may be possible for it to be wider than the 25 basis points proposed by the staff.	92	9
201407	1962	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	Several of you suggested experimenting right at the outset with a wider spread to see if the facility is even necessary to establish a floor on the funds rate.	92	9
201407	1963	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	It is conceivable that moving up IOER alone might suffice.	92	9
201407	1964	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	I have to say my own preference is to avoid experimentation on day one and instead to set the overnight RRP rate at the floor of our target range.	92	9
201407	1965	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	And, like a number of other speakers, I consider it very important, too, at the outset of the tightening process to ensure that the funds rate moves up rapidly into our new target range so that liftoff occurs smoothly.	92	9
201407	1966	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	I think after six years of near-zero interest rates, and as President Williams pointed out, chronic concerns among many that our balance sheet is simply too large for us to control short- term rates, I do believe we need to convincingly demonstrate that we, as we have long emphasized, actually have the tools and the technical expertise to control short-term interest rates.	92	9
201407	1967	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	And so I see making sure that the funds rate moves up into our new target range as important.	92	9
201407	1968	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	So to me, experimentation in those first days after policy tightening is something that could prove immensely costly.	92	9
201407	1969	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	I recognize that, conceivably, we could design our communications to explain that the initial phase of liftoff would involve experimentation and to set market expectations accordingly, not to expect a rapid move-up in the funds rate and some experimentation.	92	9
201407	1970	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	But I believe it would be very challenging.	92	9
201407	1971	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	That said, I do see the potential for experimentation to determine whether or not we can diminish the role of the facility and widen the spread as the tightening process proceeds.	92	9
201407	1972	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	And over time, I think we can consider allowing the spread to widen as a disincentive for the facility’s use.	92	9
201407	1973	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	But clearly, there are a wide range of opinions here, and I think this is an area in which more debate is probably going to be necessary before deciding what we should do.	92	9
201407	1974	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	Regarding testing, I think most of you think it’s prudent to test the new features of the overnight RRP facility later this year to prepare market participants to gain experience with the auction structure and caps.	92	9
201407	1975	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	I think I heard agreement that our other tools, like the term deposit facility, should be kept in reserve and perhaps referred to in our revised statement.	92	9
201407	1976	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	More generally, I think we all agree on the importance of maintaining flexibility as the normalization process evolves, in case we need to make adjustments along the way.	92	9
201407	1977	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	A number of you indicated that you would be willing to delegate to me, as Chair, the authority to make circumscribed or small and technical changes to administered interest rates in order to keep the effective funds rate within the target range set by the Committee, but I certainly did hear a number of you express concerns about such a delegation.	92	9
201407	1978	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	Let me be clear that if you were to delegate that decisionmaking to me, I would of course try to consult, if at all feasible, through a call or videoconference with you before making any adjustments.	92	9
201407	1979	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	And in any case, there is no doubt that we would be in close consultation during the initial stages of normalization.	92	9
201407	1980	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	Regarding communications, I think I heard general support for the revised version of the normalization principles that were circulated by staff.	92	9
201407	1981	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	There were different views on this, but I did hear quite a bit of support for the revised organization proposed by President Kocherlakota.	92	9

201407	1984	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	I very much hope that we can reach agreement on them by the time we are heading into the September meeting, with the expectation that we will be releasing them to the public with the postmeeting policy statement so that I can discuss them in the press conference.	92	9
201407	1985	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	The directive and postmeeting statements, I think I heard some expression that we are off to a good start on that.	92	9

201407	2007	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	Thank you, Madam Chair.	11	1
201407	2008	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	I’ll be referring to the one-page exhibit labeled “Material for Forecast Summary.”	11	1
201407	2009	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	Social media being all the rage these days, I thought I’d demonstrate my agility by climbing aboard a mere decade or so after the fact and try my hand at composing the Twitter version of the Tealbook that we sent you last week.	11	1
201407	2010	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	I think it would go something like this:  “US economy looks to have been running warmer than earlier thought, not cooler; we’ve extended that better trend into the future a bit.”	11	1
201407	2011	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	That’s 133 characters, including spaces, even with the typical staff qualifier “a bit.”	11	1
201407	2012	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	I could stop there, but lest you think I’m going to let you off easy, let me dash your hopes immediately.	11	1
201407	2013	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	If all you knew about the US economy lately was the information that we have about GDP growth in the first half of this year, you would probably be mighty confused by the Twitter version of the Tealbook.	11	1
201407	2014	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	After all, as you can see from the first panel of your forecast summary exhibit, the data flow since the June Tealbook points to a sizable downward revision to real GDP growth in the first half of this year, to just ¼ percent at an annual rate, 1 percentage point lower than our June projection.	11	1
201407	2015	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	To make a long story short—though not quite Twitter length—we ultimately decided to treat that reading on GDP in the first half essentially as if it were driven by measurement error and on that rationale left our growth estimates for the second half and later mostly unrevised.	11	1
201407	2016	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	Dave Stockton became famous for his remark at one of these meetings in 2004 that the staff forecast he was presenting then had a half-life shorter than a jar of mayonnaise in the Mojave Desert.	11	1
201407	2017	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	Our forecast this time could make Stockton’s look like the Moai statues on Easter Island by comparison, because we are scheduled to be proven wrong at 8:30 tomorrow morning [laughter], when the BEA will publish its first estimate of second-quarter GDP, together with the annual revision to the national accounts three years back.	11	1
201407	2018	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	In contrast to the latest readings on GDP, the news on the labor market has, on balance, surprised us to the upside.	11	1
201407	2019	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	In the establishment survey, the level of payroll employment in June was 90,000 higher than our previous Tealbook forecast.	11	1
201407	2020	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	In the household survey, as shown in panel 2 of your exhibit, the unemployment rate in June came in 0.2 percentage point below our previous projection.	11	1
201407	2021	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	Long-term unemployment has come down, initial claims for unemployment insurance benefits have been low, and job openings have moved up.	11	1
201407	2022	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	As a result, even though the labor force participation rate held steady rather than edging up as we’d projected, we judge overall labor market conditions to have improved, and our black-box summary measure of 19 labor market indicators concurs with that view.	11	1
201407	2023	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	The labor market data were not alone in pointing to a stronger pace of expansion.	11	1
201407	2024	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	For example, while the NIPA data imply a plunge in industrial-sector output in the first quarter, our own industrial production index posted a respectable gain over the same period (and the statistical evidence suggests that when such gaps have opened up in the past, the NIPA-based measure tends to correct toward the IP index rather than the other way around).	11	1
201407	2025	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	With stronger IP growth than we’d expected, second- quarter manufacturing capacity utilization is now running a little tighter than we had projected.	11	1
201407	2026	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	More broadly, business surveys including the national surveys of purchasing managers and your own regional surveys have generally been quite upbeat, not at all consistent with essentially flat GDP during the first half.	11	1
201407	2027	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	Based on these considerations, we concluded that slack in the economy is probably being taken up a little more quickly than we thought in June.	11	1
201407	2028	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	Moreover, especially in light of the repeated downside surprises in the unemployment rate that we’ve experienced over the past couple of years, we penciled in a slightly faster rate of uptake for the period ahead.	11	1
201407	2029	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	With weaker measured GDP growth but a judgment that resource utilization was running tighter than anticipated, we were compelled to adjust down our estimate of potential GDP in 2014.	11	1
201407	2030	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	The result is that we have potential GDP growth averaging zero this year.	11	1
201407	2031	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	We don’t take this estimate terribly seriously as a gauge of how quickly the sustainable capacity of the economy is expanding, but instead see it as subsuming whatever measurement error is present in GDP, thereby achieving the larger purpose of delivering to you an estimate of the output gap that better conforms with our assessment of how much economic slack remains to be taken up.	11	1
201407	2032	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	The net result is shown in panel 3, which plots the GDP gaps from the July and June Tealbooks.	11	1
201407	2033	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	As you can see, we now estimate that the GDP gap—like its unemployment-based cousin—will close about a year from now, three calendar quarters earlier than we figured in the June Tealbook.	11	1
201407	2034	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	Although the effect on medium-term GDP growth is small, I would also note that monetary policy is projected to be a little less accommodative in this forecast.	11	1
201407	2035	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	While we have maintained our assumption that asset purchases will end in the fourth quarter of this year and have likewise left in place our mechanical assumption that the federal funds rate will be set in accordance with the inertial Taylor (1999) rule starting two quarters after that, the narrower output gap in this forecast and slightly higher inflation rate cause the Taylor rule to deliver a funds rate path that is roughly 25 basis points higher than before by the end of next year and roughly 50 basis points higher by the end of 2016.	11	1
201407	2036	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	Panels 4 and 5 summarize the inflation outlook.	11	1
201407	2037	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	As you can see in panel 4, our near-term forecast calls for a little more headline PCE inflation than we previously thought.	11	1
201407	2038	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	Some of this upward revision is attributable to a higher path for food and energy prices, but the contour of futures prices leads us to expect the bulge in consumer food and energy price inflation to be relatively short-lived.	11	1
201407	2039	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	The incoming data on core PCE inflation—as shown in panel 5—have also surprised us a little to the upside.	11	1
201407	2040	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	In 2015 and 2016, we nudged up our forecast for core inflation by 0.1 percentage point, in light of the narrower margin of slack in this projection.	11	1
201407	2041	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	As in previous Tealbooks, we expect core PCE inflation to increase slowly over the projection period, from 1.6 percent this year to 1.8 percent in 2016.	11	1
201407	2042	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	Headline PCE inflation is expected to run about ¼ percentage point below the core after 2014, mostly reflecting small projected declines in consumer energy prices.	11	1
201407	2043	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	As always, numerous risks and sources of uncertainty attend our activity and inflation projections.	11	1
201407	2044	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	One characterization of this uncertainty is provided by the forecast confidence intervals that are shown in this exhibit and in the Tealbook.	11	1
201407	2045	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	But I was particularly enamored of the specific risks that were sprinkled throughout the Tealbook document, both in various boxes and in our traditional alternative simulations.	11	1
201407	2046	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	I’ve listed four of them in panel 6.	11	1
201407	2047	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	In the latest installment of our “Alternative View” franchise, Eric Engen and Michael Palumbo highlight the possibility that the economy could be persistently stuck in a low-growth expectations trap, and that a dramatic change in policy regime may be required to jolt the expansion onto a more satisfactory trajectory.	11	1
201407	2048	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	In the “Risks and Uncertainty” section of the Tealbook, a pair of scenarios attempts to bookend the risks around our assessment of resource utilization.	11	1
201407	2049	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	In the one labeled “Stronger Activity with Higher Inflation,” we posit a world in which the unemployment rate continues to decline more in line with its recent pace rather than flattening out as we have it in the baseline, and inflation proves at the same time more sensitive to the increase in resource utilization.	11	1
201407	2050	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	Alternatively, in the scenario labeled “Weaker Household Demand,” we examine the possibility that the first-quarter readings on GDP and GDI turn out to be sending the truer signal about the momentum of the expansion, and that a substantially more accommodative stance of policy will be required to achieve your dual mandate.	11	1
201407	2051	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	And, to illustrate the role that model uncertainty plays in our assessment of potential risks, we included a box in the Tealbook that analyzed the consequences of a disruption to credit markets using both FRB/US and a DSGE model with financial frictions.	11	1
201407	2052	2014-07-30	meeting	WILCOX	While we cannot claim that these various alternatives exhaust—or even bound—the full set of outcomes that are possible over the next few years, we do think that they provide a reasonable indication of the considerable uncertainty that we face as forecasters and that you face as policymakers.	11	1

201407	2063	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	As indicated in panel 2, the pothole was concentrated in the emerging market economies, or EMEs, as growth in China, other emerging Asian economies, and Brazil slowed sharply, while the Mexican economy continued to languish.	11	1
201407	2064	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	In the absence of clear and fundamental drivers of the slowdown, we judged the soft patch to be temporary.	11	1
201407	2065	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	In the event, the data received since your previous meeting have generally borne out our forecast.	11	1
201407	2066	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	Perhaps most importantly, Chinese GDP growth has picked up from 5½ percent in the first quarter to an estimated 7¾ percent in the second, even stronger than we’d projected, as the trade surplus bounced back and the economy responded to a steady stream of fiscal and monetary stimulus measures.	11	1
201407	2067	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	Partly as a result, activity in most of China’s emerging market neighbors also appears to have accelerated.	11	1
201407	2068	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	Meanwhile, on this side of the Pacific, we estimate the Mexican economy shook off its year-long torpor and grew at 3 percent in the second quarter as US manufacturing demand picked up, the effect of prior tax hikes waned, and a long-standing slump in construction began to ease.	11	1
201407	2069	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	All told, the rate of expansion in the EMEs bounced back to over 3½ percent in the second quarter.	11	1
201407	2070	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	Assuming that the United States and other advanced economies perform as projected, EME growth should level out next year at its trend pace of slightly below 4½ percent.	11	1
201407	2071	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	As shown in panel 3, the advanced foreign economies appear to have experienced a mini-pothole of their own in the second quarter.	11	1
201407	2072	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	However, this was largely an expected consequence of the April consumption tax hike in Japan, which is estimated to have lowered GDP more than 5 percent.	11	1
201407	2073	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	The most recent data on consumer spending and manufacturing for Japan have been reasonably favorable, and we believe Japanese GDP will start growing again in the current quarter.	11	1
201407	2074	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	With Canada having shaken off the effects of an unusually harsh winter and the UK economy slated to continue its solid expansion, the main question for the advanced foreign economies centers around the euro area.	11	1
201407	2075	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	Recent economic performance in the euro area has been decidedly mixed, and credit conditions remain tight.	11	1
201407	2076	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	Accordingly, we continue to project rather weak, sub– 2 percent growth for the region.	11	1
201407	2077	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	Even so, we think it likely that the recovery will stay more or less on track.	11	1
201407	2078	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	For starters, we do not anticipate the region falling into deflation, though that remains a risk.	11	1
201407	2079	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	Substantial resource slack and falling retail energy prices have pushed the 12-month inflation rate down to a dismally low ½ percent, but energy prices are rising again, and as the output gap narrows, overall inflation should pick up as well.	11	1
201407	2080	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	Nor do we see the troubles with Portugal’s Banco Espírito Santo, described by Simon in his briefing, as threatening substantial disruptions.	11	1
201407	2081	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	The bank is quite small—accounting for less than ½ percent of the total assets of euro-area banks—and its problems appear too idiosyncratic to trigger contagion to other institutions.	11	1
201407	2082	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	Outside of the euro area, the main risks to our forecast of solid but unspectacular foreign growth appear to be in the emerging market economies.	11	1
201407	2083	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	Coming a little more than a year after the start of the taper tantrum, this struck us as a good time to assess whether the likelihood of one key risk—a deep and broad-based EME financial crisis—has risen or declined.	11	1
201407	2084	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	All told, the results of our assessment are mixed.	11	1
201407	2085	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	Panel 4 displays our index of the fundamental vulnerabilities of the 13 EMEs we track closely.	11	1
201407	2086	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	This index improved only a touch between 2013 and 2014, and not at all for the so-called fragile five EMEs.	11	1
201407	2087	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	Despite this lack of significant progress on fundamentals, however, EMBI credit spreads, the red line in panel 5, have now returned to their pre–taper tantrum levels.	11	1
201407	2088	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	This raises the question of whether investors have again become too complacent about EME risks, increasing the likelihood of disruptive corrections down the road.	11	1
201407	2089	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	All that said, we see some reasons for judging the glass to be half full rather than half empty.	11	1
201407	2090	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	To begin with, as shown by the blue line in panel 5, the share of investment-fund assets devoted to EMEs declined after May of last year and remains subdued, despite some pickup from earlier this year.	11	1
201407	2091	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	As shown in panel 6, real effective exchange rates for the fragile five are now lower than they were at the start of the taper tantrum.	11	1
201407	2092	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	This depreciation should bolster investor confidence by reducing current account deficits, strengthening growth, and muting expectations that further depreciation will be needed in the future.	11	1
201407	2093	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	Finally, as indicated in panel 7, central banks in the most vulnerable economies have raised their policy rates, albeit to varying extents, over the past year, which should help tamp down inflation, support currency values, and thus also instill confidence.	11	1
201407	2094	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	Nevertheless, these improvements are not enough to take off the table the risk of a widespread EME crisis.	11	1
201407	2095	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	One possible trigger for such a crisis is the normalization of monetary policies in the United States and other advanced economies.	11	1
201407	2096	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	It is not clear why such a highly anticipated event should disrupt global financial markets, but we cannot be certain that markets are fully pricing in the future paths of advanced- economy monetary policies.	11	1
201407	2097	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	Another possible trigger would be a hard landing in China.	11	1
201407	2098	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	Due to its increasing prominence as an importer of both primary commodities and intermediate manufactures, a financial crisis and resultant sharp economic slowdown in China could have severe ramifications for the emerging market economies more generally.	11	1
201407	2099	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	In the QS Assessment of Financial Stability that was distributed to the FOMC last week, we considered two China-crisis scenarios, depicted in your next exhibit.	11	1
201407	2100	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	In the first scenario, a crisis and recession lower Chinese GDP growth to only 2 percent in 2015.	11	1
201407	2101	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	In turn, as shown by the green line in panel 1, spillovers through normal trade and commodity price channels lead to a sharp slowing of aggregate EME growth; as shown in panel 2, this leads to a discernable but limited hit to US activity.	11	1
201407	2102	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	In the second scenario, depicted by the red lines in both panels, China’s hard landing not only spills abroad through standard trade channels, but it also induces a surge in investor risk aversion that triggers financial crises in many EMEs and severe disruptions in the United States and other advanced-economy markets.	11	1
201407	2103	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	In this scenario, which was also presented in the Tealbook, growth falls by considerably more in both the United States and the EMEs.	11	1
201407	2104	2014-07-30	meeting	KAMIN	On this happy note, David Bowman will continue our presentation.	11	1
201407	2105	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	Thank you.	11	1
201407	2106	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	I will be providing an overview of the QS Assessment of Financial Stability.	FS	FS
201407	2107	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	We continue to see the overall vulnerability of the financial system as moderate, given the slow growth of credit within the nonfinancial sector and the relatively strong capital positions of US banks and subdued use of maturity transformation and leverage within the financial system.	FS	FS
201407	2108	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	Nevertheless, low and declining risk premiums and loosening standards in a number of markets raise the possibility of an eventual correction in asset valuations.	FS	FS
201407	2109	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	The pattern of steadily declining spreads on riskier assets has continued since April.	FS	FS
201407	2110	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	I’ll begin with a review of corporate debt markets.	FS	FS
201407	2111	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	As shown by the black line in panel 1 in the handout titled “Material for Briefing on Financial Stability Developments,” spreads on high-yield corporate bonds have fallen a bit further over the past few months, despite a recent uptick.	FS	FS
201407	2112	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	The red line, which adjusts for a staff estimate of expected default, indicates that risk premiums in this market have also declined, but they still remain above their lowest levels in the late 1990s.	FS	FS
201407	2113	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	Issuance of high-yield debt, the dark blue bars in the panel to the right, has continued to be robust, as has issuance of leveraged loans, the light blue bars.	FS	FS
201407	2114	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	Roughly half of the recently issued high-yield bonds and institutional leveraged loans are being used for purposes other than refinancing, and underwriting standards have continued to weaken.	FS	FS
201407	2115	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	For example, the debt multiples involved in recent leveraged buyout deals, shown in dark blue in the middle-left panel, have edged above their levels in 2005 and 2006, although as shown by the red line, the equity stake in these deals has been relatively stable.	FS	FS
201407	2116	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	More broadly, despite the Federal Reserve’s guidance, we have thus far seen no evidence that banks have in aggregate pulled back from originating riskier deals or that activity is shifting significantly to nonbank lenders.	FS	FS
201407	2117	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	In equity markets, prices have increased a further 6 percent since April, but while certain sectors may be overstretched, we have less concern about the equity market as a whole.	FS	FS
201407	2118	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	As seen to the right, the staff estimate of the equity premium, in red, is still reasonably high.	FS	FS
201407	2119	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	In contrast, the VIX index of implied volatility in the S&P 500, shown in black in the bottom-left panel, is quite low, but our concerns about this are to some extent ameliorated by the fact that realized and implied volatilities generally tend to be low during economic recoveries and that options at longer maturities indicate a still-healthy price of longer-term downside risk.	FS	FS
201407	2120	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	For example, the red line in the panel measures the price of insuring against a 10 percent decline in stock prices over the next year and has been fairly steady near its long-term average over the past two years.	FS	FS
201407	2121	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	Even so, the near uniformity of declines in short-term implied volatilities across markets may reflect an underpricing of risk and some complacency on the part of market participants.	FS	FS
201407	2122	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	The black line to the right shows that a composite index of implied volatilities across global equities, rates, currencies, and commodities is at an all-time low, and it is difficult to fathom why implied volatilities for oil, the red line, should be so low when Iraq is in an internal war, tensions with Russia are elevated, and Israel and Hamas are in open conflict.	FS	FS
201407	2123	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	Your next exhibit discusses the factors that contribute to our assessment that, despite these apparent signs of valuation pressures in some markets, the overall vulnerability of the financial system is judged to be moderate.	FS	FS
201407	2124	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	While leverage ratios for speculative-grade and unrated firms, the red line in the top-left panel, are above average levels, overall leverage in the nonfinancial business sector as a whole, shown in black, remains low by historical standards.	FS	FS
201407	2125	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	In addition, net borrowing by prime and superprime households, shown in the panel to the right, has risen only modestly in recent quarters, and there has been no net borrowing by subprime households.	FS	FS
201407	2126	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	The banking sector is also in relatively strong shape.	FS	FS
201407	2127	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	Reliance on wholesale funding by large bank holding companies, the black line in the middle-left panel, is substantially lower than in the mid-2000s, while Tier 1 common capital ratios (the red line) have continued to increase.	FS	FS
201407	2128	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	In addition, leverage in other parts of the financial sector appears to be fairly stable.	FS	FS
201407	2129	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	For example, as shown in the panel to the right, dealer responses to the most recent SCOOS indicate that the use of leverage by some of their clients—hedge funds, real estate investment trusts, mutual funds, and exchange-traded funds—has changed little in recent months.	FS	FS
201407	2130	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	That said, separate data from prime brokers suggest that the use of leverage by hedge funds remains elevated, and overall levels of securitization, while still moderate, have been picking up especially in CLOs and to some extent CMBS.	FS	FS
201407	2131	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	While we take comfort from the relatively low levels of maturity transformation and leverage, any market correction could be magnified by sales of relatively illiquid assets.	FS	FS
201407	2132	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	As shown in the bottom-left panel, flows into mutual funds investing in less liquid assets, including corporate and emerging market debt, have continued to increase.	FS	FS
201407	2133	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	As we have discussed before, most of those flows began during the recovery and there is a danger that investors are ill prepared to expect potential losses and that they might pull out rapidly if a downturn occurred.	FS	FS
201407	2134	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	In addition, data from the CFTC (not shown) suggest that some institutional investors are taking long positions in interest rate derivatives, increasing their exposures to rate risk.	FS	FS
201407	2135	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	These risks would be compounded if term premiums in Treasury bonds, shown to the right, were to rebound or if market participants were to substantially increase their expectations for the future path of short-term rates.	FS	FS
201407	2136	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	Your last exhibit provides a summary of our overall assessment and of current policy initiatives.	FS	FS
201407	2137	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	As noted, although we consider the risk of a correction to have increased given the downward momentum in and comparatively low levels of risk premiums in some markets, we believe that the overall vulnerability of the financial system remains moderate given the fairly strong positions of household and corporate balance sheets and the relatively contained use of maturity transformation and leverage by the financial sector.	FS	FS
201407	2138	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	Nonetheless, the current environment of low volatility and low risk premiums may encourage greater risk-taking and leverage , and we will remain attuned to any deterioration.	FS	FS
201407	2139	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	On the policy front, the staff continues to pursue initiatives related to the specific vulnerabilities that we have identified.	FS	FS
201407	2140	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	Regarding leveraged loans, public data suggest that the terms and structures of new deals have continued to deteriorate despite the issuance of guidance and follow-up supervisory letters last year.	FS	FS
201407	2141	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	Currently, supervisors are engaged in completing the Shared National Credit (SNC) examinations, which are heavily focused on leveraged loans and the degree to which domestic and foreign banks are complying with the guidance.	FS	FS
201407	2142	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	The findings of the SNC exams are expected to be available in mid-August for the purposes of providing feedback to firms.	FS	FS
201407	2143	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	Regarding the potential effects on banks of a sharp rebound in interest rates, the staff is conducting a study of interest rate risk at six of the largest bank holding companies.	FS	FS
201407	2144	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	Firms were asked to revalue their trading books in a number of different scenarios for interest rates, and information also was gathered on the counterparties to these risk exposures.	FS	FS
201407	2145	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	This work should be able to both identify banks’ vulnerabilities and determine whether there are any key counterparties who have built up significant interest rate risk exposures with one or more of these banks.	FS	FS
201407	2146	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	Regarding flows into funds and less liquid assets, we are also continuing work with the FSB and IOSCO in understanding the risks related to exchange-traded funds under stressed market conditions.	FS	FS
201407	2147	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	Finally, last week the SEC issued a rule to reform money market funds.	FS	FS
201407	2148	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	The rule mandates that, within about two years, prime institutional funds float their net asset values, or NAVs.	FS	FS
201407	2149	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	The rule also contains provisions for the discretionary imposition of gates or redemption fees by fund boards in the event that a fund faces severe liquidity pressures.	FS	FS
201407	2150	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	The staff views the floating NAV requirement as a step forward but is concerned that discretionary fees and gates could be destabilizing.	FS	FS
201407	2151	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	The net effect for financial stability could depend, in part, on the extent to which the more run-prone institutional investors move away from prime money funds to other cash- management strategies, and the risks that may be posed by those strategies.	FS	FS
201407	2152	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	The Financial Stability Oversight Council currently is reviewing the proposal.	FS	FS
201407	2153	2014-07-30	meeting	BOWMAN	That concludes our remarks.	FS	FS

201407	2302	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	While it’s well understood that monetary policy operates with long and variable lags, as we think about financial-stability issues and the potential substitutability or complementarity of supervisory and monetary tools, it’s important to remind ourselves that long and variable lags are just as applicable to our supervisory tools, particularly given the long lags that frequently occur in instituting new rules.	FS	FS
201407	2303	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	For example, the draft guidance on leveraged lending was released for public comment in March 2012.	FS	FS
201407	2304	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Two years later a number of institutions, particularly some of the foreign institutions, are still reluctant to address the concerns raised in the guidance.	FS	FS
201407	2305	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Given the importance of this market segment to the business model of some foreign banks, it’s not a complete surprise they are reluctant to tighten standards in an area that generates substantial fees.	FS	FS
201407	2306	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	There are probably ways we can shorten the timeline in regulatory and supervisory tools and be more creative in writing rules that provide more flexibility to make changes without going through additional rounds of comments.	FS	FS
201407	2307	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Still, this very recent experience certainly raises the question of whether we have fully considered how promptly we can address financial- stability concerns and which tools will be most timely and effective.	FS	FS
201407	2308	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	In a similar vein, we should consider how we would address the problems currently facing the Bank of England and the Riksbank regarding real estate prices.	FS	FS
201407	2309	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Choice of homebuyers would be influenced by higher rates generated by monetary policy, higher interest rates generated by imposing higher capital charges on banks through bank regulation, or higher underwriting standards through bank supervision.	FS	FS
201407	2310	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	While I don’t expect that this is an immediate area of concern, it may be an area in which considering the tradeoffs between relying on monetary policy tools or relying on supervisory or regulatory tools would be particularly instructive.	FS	FS
201407	2311	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	In principle, we could use targeted monetary policy tools to address real estate excesses, such as selling long-term mortgages, MBS, or Treasury securities to directly raise mortgage and other long-term rates.	FS	FS
201407	2312	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Our ability to use such tools will be influenced by our decisions about how long-run balance sheet size and composition are decided.	FS	FS
201407	2313	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	But such decisions should also be informed by how confident we are that supervisory or regulatory tools will be effective in addressing some of the issues already being confronted elsewhere.	FS	FS

201407	2385	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	One risk that the QS report doesn’t focus on, because it’s a pretty narrow risk, is the situation in Puerto Rico, and since that sits in our District I thought I would comment on it.	FS	FS
201407	2386	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	Unfortunately, the island economy has been essentially in recession for years, and during this period there’s been a rapid buildup in the debt burden of the island, particularly among the public corporations that are there.	FS	FS
201407	2387	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	As a result, the island is losing market access.	FS	FS
201407	2388	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	There was a large general obligation issuance this spring that was funded mainly by hedge funds at around an 8 percent yield.	FS	FS
201407	2389	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	So that sort of tells you the degree of extremis.	FS	FS
201407	2390	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	Recently the government attempted to differentiate between the obligations of the commonwealth and the obligations of the public corporations by passing bankruptcy legislation that would apply only to the public corporations.	FS	FS
201407	2391	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	This did not work in achieving the desired differentiation.	FS	FS
201407	2392	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	The rating agencies downgraded both the government and the public corporate obligations.	FS	FS
201407	2393	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	Also, utilizing this new law and putting a public corporation into bankruptcy doesn’t seem to be viable in fact, because there’s legal uncertainty about how such a bankruptcy filing would work, given the absence of legal precedents.	FS	FS
201407	2394	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	We also have a situation of liquidity being drained.	FS	FS
201407	2395	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	They made this big bond issuance, but the liquidity is getting exhausted relatively quickly, both seasonally—because tax receipts in Puerto Rico are back-loaded in the fiscal year, and the fiscal year starts July 1—and by the fact that energy suppliers to the island’s public utility are demanding much tougher trade terms.	FS	FS
201407	2396	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	So what’s happening is the government is trying to negotiate a restructuring of the public utility company’s obligations, and if that were to succeed, it would provide some additional liquid resources and buy some time.	FS	FS
201407	2397	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	Also, it will be very important to see if the government could actually issue tax anticipation notes, which it typically does this time of year.	FS	FS
201407	2398	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	If it can’t do this and it can’t do the public utility restructuring, then the cushion of liquid resources may not be adequate to meet its obligations for very much longer.	FS	FS
201407	2399	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	So the bottom line is, the outlook is pretty grim.	FS	FS
201407	2400	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	If things go well, so that they get the public utility restructuring and the government issues tax anticipation notes, that will probably get them into next year, but if those efforts fail, then Puerto Rico might be either unable or unwilling to meet its obligations much sooner.	FS	FS
201407	2401	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	There are over $70 billion of tax-exempt securities outstanding from Puerto Rico—both the government and the public corporations.	FS	FS
201407	2402	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	So if this thing sped up, this would be a pretty significant shock to the US tax-exempt market.	FS	FS
201407	2403	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	That said, I do think even if this worst case were to occur, the systemic effect probably would be pretty modest in the sense that the Puerto Rico situation does appear to be quite unique.	FS	FS

201407	2413	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	Many more market participants favor rising stock prices than the opposite.	FS	FS
201407	2414	2014-07-30	meeting	DUDLEY	[Laughter]	FS	FS

201407	2500	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	On balance, recent reports on economic activity in the Fifth District have been fairly positive.	13	1

201407	2503	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	A typical comment comes from a bank CEO, who recently stated that his bank has been experiencing organic loan growth this year for the first time in five years.	13	1

201407	2507	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Contacts in the Hampton Roads area of southeast Virginia and elsewhere are also concerned about prospective defense cuts that could have a large effect locally.	13	1
201407	2508	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Turning to the national outlook, the staff has lowered its forecast for consumer spending significantly for 2014 and trimmed a bit off of 2015 and 2016, as we’ve heard.	13	1

201407	2523	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Two meetings ago I talked about the labor market, since we were about to drop our forward guidance referring to numerical thresholds for the unemployment rate.	13	1
201407	2524	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	For this meeting, we are considering a statement that shifts the emphasis away from the standard unemployment rate and toward other labor market indicators.	13	1
201407	2525	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	This is consistent with our general practice of considering the broadest possible range of data, as well as our continuing struggle to assess labor market conditions in the wake of the Great Recession.	13	1
201407	2526	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	We’ve been worried about the unusually large increase in long-term unemployment, the declining labor force participation rate, and the relatively high numbers of people working part time for economic reasons.	13	1
201407	2527	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	At the previous meeting I argued that despite these unusual developments, the unemployment rate still seems to be a good summary statistic for the current state of the labor market.	13	1
201407	2528	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	At this meeting I want to describe briefly a little bit of additional research on this question.	13	1
201407	2529	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	One simple way to approach this is to look at the joint behavior of an extended unemployment measure such as U-6, which includes both marginally attached workers and people working part time for economic reasons, with the standard unemployment rate, U-3.	13	1
201407	2530	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	The U-6 measure is greater than U-3, obviously, but if you look at a scatter plot with U-6 on the vertical axis and U-3 on the horizontal axis, you see a very tight linear relationship for unemployment rates below 7 percent.	13	1
201407	2531	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Since the Great Recession, however, there’s been an apparent upward shift in that relationship.	13	1
201407	2532	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Any given value of the standard unemployment rate has been associated with a higher value of U-6 than in the past, and right now the gap is about 1.6 percentage points.	13	1
201407	2533	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	And this fact supports the view that there is now more labor market underutilization than is typically associated with an unemployment rate of 6.1 percent.	13	1
201407	2534	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	I want to make a couple of observations.	13	1
201407	2535	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	First, this apparent gap does not seem to be related to marginally attached workers, since for U-5 the current values lie along the relationship that was displayed before the Great Recession.	13	1
201407	2536	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Second, part-time workers are by definition working more than zero hours per week.	13	1
201407	2537	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	In fact, from the CPS, it looks like the average is about 23 hours per week.	13	1
201407	2538	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	As a result, a measure like U-6, in which a part-time worker counts the same as an unemployed worker, is biased upward as a measure of labor market underutilization.	13	1
201407	2539	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Part-time workers who would like to work full time are underutilized only to the extent that their hours worked would increase if they had the job they desired.	13	1
201407	2540	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	This suggests that in a good measure of labor market utilization, the proper weight for people working part time for economic reasons would be less than one.	13	1
201407	2541	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	In the CPS, the average weekly hours of part-time workers are about half the average weekly hours of full-time workers.	13	1
201407	2542	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	So the number of people working part time for economic reasons should get a weight of one-half, and if you adjust U-6 this way, you significantly reduce the extent to which it’s unusually high now.	13	1
201407	2543	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	In fact, you cut it almost in half.	13	1
201407	2544	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	In April, I discussed research on this topic by Richmond Fed economists.	13	1
201407	2545	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	What they did is take this reasoning to its logical conclusion.	13	1
201407	2546	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	They constructed a comprehensive index of labor market underutilization that includes all nonemployed adults.	13	1
201407	2547	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	The phrase “unemployment index” was already taken, so they call it the “nonemployment index.”	13	1
201407	2548	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Different groups are weighted by their likelihood of transitioning from their group to employment relative to the transition rate observed for the short-term unemployed.	13	1
201407	2549	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	So the long-term unemployed have about half the transition rate of the short-term unemployed.	13	1
201407	2550	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Those who are marginally attached are actually about the same as the long-term unemployed, with about half the transition rate of the short-term unemployed.	13	1
201407	2551	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	This seems like one of the most straightforward ways you could think of to construct a quantitative measure of labor market utilization that takes into account people out of the labor market who might transition back into the workforce as demand picks up.	13	1
201407	2552	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	It weights them by the historical odds of them making that kind of transition.	13	1
201407	2553	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	This nonemployment index turns out to be right in line with what’s usually associated with the current level of the standard unemployment rate.	13	1
201407	2554	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	In other words, it’s close to equal to the level of the index displayed in the past, before this recession, at times at which U-3 was 6.1 percent.	13	1
201407	2555	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	So this, to me, suggests that we ought to be a bit cautious about shifting the emphasis from the unemployment rate to some other labor market indicators, since they all seem to be pointing in about the same direction regarding the improvement in labor market outcomes.	13	1
201407	2556	2014-07-30	meeting	LACKER	Thank you.	13	1
201407	2557	2014-07-30	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	13	1

201407	2570	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, given that I and others have been overpredicting real GDP growth for some time, I will need to see signs that the pickup is really happening this time before I can have much confidence in that outlook.	13	1
201407	2571	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	I would note that the models we run in Boston have been expecting stronger residential investment and consumption than has occurred.	13	1

201407	2573	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	With actual spending significantly below these target levels, the equations imply an acceleration of growth in the forecast as residential investment and consumption catch up to their target levels.	13	1
201407	2574	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, there’s an alternative explanation that is becoming more difficult to dismiss.	13	1
201407	2575	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Consumers and homebuyers may have become more risk-averse as a result of the financial crisis, or they may have significantly revised down their perceptions of lifetime resources.	13	1
201407	2576	2014-07-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	In this scenario, the desired or target levels of consumption and residential investment, whose estimates cannot yet adequately capture this structural change, may be too optimistic.	13	1
